Amm and Khass — General and Specific
beginner
12 min
The First Division of Words: Khass, 'Amm, Mushtarak, Mu'awwal
Introducing the four types of words and their definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the four word types (khass, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal) and state their definitions as given in the first division of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Words are divided by their placement into four types based on whether they indicate one meaning or more.

In usul al-fiqh, the first step in analyzing divine texts is understanding how words convey meaning. This lesson introduces the foundational classification of words based on their original linguistic placement (al-wad'). This division into four categories—al-khass, al-'amm, al-mushtarak, and al-mu'awwal—underpins all later discussions of textual interpretation and legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the basis of division
Understand that the first division considers the word's placement for meaning, disregarding usage and clarity. The commentator emphasizes that the division is based on induction (istiqra') from language, not pure reason.
2
Distinguish single from multiple meaning
Identify whether the word indicates one meaning or more than one. If one meaning, proceed to step 3; if multiple, proceed to step 4.
3
For single meaning: differentiate khass and 'amm
If the word indicates a single meaning with individualness (al-infiraad) relative to individuals, it is khass. If it indicates a single meaning with sharing (al-ishtiraak) among individuals, it is 'amm.
Note that 'amm does not require actual multiple individuals; it is defined by the capacity for sharing.
4
For multiple meanings: differentiate mushtarak and mu'awwal
If the word indicates multiple meanings with no preponderance by virtue of placement, it is mushtarak. If one meaning is made preponderant through interpretation (ta'wil) by a mujtahid, it is mu'awwal. However, mu'awwal is in reality a subtype of mushtarak.
5
Apply to examples
Given a word, classify it into one of the four categories. For instance, 'rajul' (man) is khass, 'rijal' (men) is 'amm, 'qur'' (menstruation or purity) is mushtarak, and after Hanafi interpretation 'qur'' becomes mu'awwal for hayd.

مبحث الكتاب
التقسيم الأول باعتبار وضع اللفظ للمعنى
وإنما قال: أقسامهما ولم يقل: أقسامه؛ تنبيها على أن منشأ التقسيم هو النظم والمعنى جميعًا، فبعضهم على أن التقسيمات الثلاثة الأول للنظم والرابع للمعنى، وبعضهم على أن الدلالة والاقتضاء للمعنى والبواقي للنظم، والأصح أنه في كل قسم يراعى النظم مع دلالته على المعنى. وذلك أربعة أي المذكور فيما قبل وهو التقسيمات أربعة تقسيمات، وتحت كل تقسيم منها أقسام عديدة كما سيأتي؛ وذلك لأن البحث فيه إما أن يكون عن المعنى وهو الكتاب التقسيم الرابع، أو عن اللفظ، فإما بحسب استعماله وهو التقسيم الثالث، أو بحسب دلالته، فإن اعتبر فيها الظهور والخفاء فهو الثاني، وإلا فهو الأول. على المعنى التقسيم الأول باعتبار وضع اللفظ للمعنى الأول في وجوه النظم صيغة ولغة يعني أن التقسيم الأول في طرق النظم من حيث الصيغة واللغة والطرق هي الأنواع والأصناف أي الأقسام النظم والمعنى جميعًا أراد به النظم الدال على المعنى بقرينة قوله الآتي: والأصح إلخ. (القمر) أن الدلالة والاقتضاء إلخ فإن المستدل إن لم يستدل بالنظم بل بالمعنى فإن كان المعنى مفهوما منه لغة فهو دلالة النص، وإلا فإن توقف عليه صحة النظم شرعًا، أو عقلاً فهو اقتضاء النص. (القمر) يراعى إلخ أخذا بالحاصل وميلاً إلى الضبط. (القمر) أي المذكور إلخ تصريح للمشار إليه دفعا لما يتوهم من أن ذلك للإشارة إلى مذكر مفرد والمشار إليه ههنا التقسيمات وهو جمع مؤنث. (القمر) أربعة تقسيمات إيماء إلى أن التنوين في قول المصنف : أربعة عوض عن المضاف إليه، ثم اعلم أن هذا الحصر بالاستقراء، وليس عقليًا دائرًا بين النفي والإثبات. (القمر) وذلك إلخ وجه للضبط في الأربعة. (القمر) استعماله: أي في المعنى الموضوع له أو غيره . (القمر) فيها الظهور :إلخ أي في الدلالة ظهور المعنى وخفاؤه. (القمر) في طرق النظم إلخ هذا دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن المتبادر من الوجوه الدلائل؛ لأنه جمع وجه، ومعنى الوجه في العرف الدليل، ولا يذكر في هذا التقسيم دليل شيء من النظم ،والمعنى فأجاب: بأن الوجوه ههنا بمعنى الطرق؛ لأن الوجه في وجه الشيء بمعنى طريقه، ومنه سمي الوجه وجها؛ لكونه طريقا إلى معرفة صاحبه، والمراد من الوجوه الأقسام والأنواع. (السنبلي)
التقسيم الأول باعتبار وضع اللفظ للمعنى
والصيغة هي الهيأة، واللغة وإن كان يشمل المادة والهيأة كليهما لكن أريد بها ههنا: المادة؛ للمقابلة فهما من حيث المجموع كناية عن الوضع فكأنه قال: الأول في أنواع النظم من حيث أي بين الصيغة واللغة المعنى الوضع أي من حيث أنه وضع لمعنى واحد أو أكثر مع قطع النظر عن استعماله وظهوره، وإنما قدم الصيغة على اللغة؛ لأن للعموم والخصوص زيادة تعلق بالصيغة في الأغلب. وهي أربعة الخاص والعام والمشترك والمؤول؛ لأن اللفظ إمّا أن يدل على معنى واحد أو أكثر، فإن كان الأول : فإما أن يدل على الانفراد عن الأفراد فهو الخاص، أو أن يدل مع الاشتراك بين الأفراد فهو العام، وإن كان الثاني : فإما أن يترجح أحد معانيه أي الدلالة على أكثر بالوضع بالتأويل فهو المؤول، وإلا فهو المشترك، فالمؤول في الحقيقة إنما هو من أقسام المشترك الذي دل صيغةً ولغةً وإن كان مفعول فعل التأويل الذي من شأن المجتهد. أي على المعنى الكثيرة الهيأة أي الحاصلة للفظ باعتبار التصرف وقيل باعتبار ترتيب الحروف والحركات والسكنات. (القمر) وإن كان يشمل إلخ فإن اللغة هو اللفظ الموضوع. (القمر) كناية إلخ لأن المادة أي جوهر الحروف من حيث هي هي لم توجد موضوعة لشيء، وإنما وضعت بشرط الاقتران بالهيأة جزئيةً كانت كهيأة رجل، أو كليّةً كهيأة ضرب فيلاحظ كلاهما في الوضع. (القمر) زيادة تعلق إلخ فإن التفرقة بين الرجل والرجال بأن الأول خاص، والثاني عام ثبتت بالصيغة، لا بالمادة، فإن مادتهما واحدة وما قيل من أن المقصود من الكلام إفهام السامع، والسَّامع لا يفهم بدون الصيغة، ففيه أن هذا إنما يدل على أن للصيغة دخلا في الإفهام لا على أن للعموم والخصوص زيادة تعلق بالصيغة فتأمل. (القمر) وهي: أي وجوه النظم ولا حاجة إلى ما في "مسير "الدائر" من الضمير راجع إلى الأول والتأنيث باعتبار الخبر.(القمر) على الانفراد أي مع قطع النظر عن أن يكون له في الخارج أفراد أو لم يكن، وخرج به العام، فإنه يتناول أفرادا على ما سيجيء . (القمر) فالمؤول إلخ إيراد على جعل المصنف المؤول قسيما للمشترك. (القمر) إنما هو من أقسام إلخ: ومن ههنا تتفطن أن المؤول قسم من النظم صيغةً ولغةً، فإن قسم القسم قسم، كيف وأن لفظ المشترك كالقرء قبل التأويل يدل على أحد المعنيين بالوضع، وبعد التأويل لم يتغير تلك الدلالة الوضعية بل يتعين كالحيض عندنا والطهر عند الشافعي (القمر)
Section on the Book (Mabahith al-Kitab): The First Division: Considering the placement of the word for the meaning. And he said: 'their divisions' and did not say 'its divisions' as a hint that the origin of the division is the wording (nazm) and the meaning together. Some say the first three divisions are for the wording and the fourth for the meaning; some say that indication (dalala) and implication (iqtida') are for the meaning and the rest for the wording; and the correct view is that in every division, the wording is considered along with its indication of the meaning. And those are four: meaning what was mentioned previously, i.e., the divisions are four, and under each division are numerous subdivisions as will come. That is because the research is either about the meaning, which is the fourth division, or about the word. If about the word, then either according to its usage, which is the third division, or according to its indication; if in that indication both clarity and hiddenness are considered, then it is the second division; otherwise it is the first division. The first division: considering the placement of the word for the meaning. The first regarding the aspects of wording (nazm): form (sigha) and language (lugha). Meaning that the first division concerns the ways of wording from the perspective of form and language; and the ways are the types and kinds, i.e., the divisions. 'Wording and meaning together': he intended the wording that indicates the meaning, based on the context of his subsequent statement 'and the correct view etc.' (al-Qamar). 'That indication and implication etc.': for if the one seeking proof does not use the wording but rather the meaning, then if the meaning is understood from it linguistically, it is 'indication of the text' (dalalat al-nass); otherwise, if the validity of the wording depends on it legally or rationally, it is 'implication of the text' (iqtida' al-nass). (al-Qamar). 'Is considered etc.': taking the result and inclining toward precision. (al-Qamar). 'Meaning what was mentioned etc.': a clarification of the referent, to repel the misunderstanding that the pronoun refers to a masculine singular, whereas the referent here is 'al-taqsimat' which is a feminine plural. (al-Qamar). 'Four divisions': insinuating that the tanwin in the author's statement 'four' substitutes for the annexed noun. Then know that this enumeration is by induction (istiqra'), not rational (aqlan) revolving between negation and affirmation. (al-Qamar). 'And that etc.': a reason for precision in the four. (al-Qamar). 'Its usage': i.e., in the meaning for which it was placed or other than that. (al-Qamar). 'In it clarity etc.': i.e., in the indication: clarity of the meaning and its hiddenness. (al-Qamar). 'In the ways of wording etc.': this answers a hypothetical objection: that the apparent meaning of 'wujuh' is 'proofs', because it is a plural of 'wajh', and the meaning of 'wajh' in common usage is 'proof', and nothing is mentioned in this division about proof of wording and meaning. So he replied: 'wujuh' here is in the sense of 'ways', because 'wajh' in 'wajh of a thing' means its way; hence the face is called 'wajh' because it is a way to recognize its owner. What is meant by 'wujuh' are the divisions and types. (al-Sunbuli). The first division: considering the placement of the word for the meaning. And 'sigha' (form) is the form (hay'a), and 'lugha' (language) although it includes both the substance (madda) and the form, here what is intended is the substance, for the sake of contrast. So, collectively, they are a metonym for 'placement' (wad'). So it is as if he said: the first is regarding the types of wording from the perspective of placement, i.e., that it is placed for one meaning or more, regardless of its usage and clarity. And he presented 'sigha' over 'lugha' because generality and specificity are more related to form in most cases. And they are four: the specific (al-khass), the general (al-'amm), the shared (al-mushtarak), and the interpreted (al-mu'awwal). Because the word either indicates one meaning or more. If the first: then either it indicates individualness relative to individuals, so it is specific; or it indicates with sharing among individuals, so it is general. If the second: then either one of its meanings is preponderant by placement through interpretation, so it is interpreted; otherwise, it is shared. So the interpreted in reality is only one of the divisions of the shared word, which indicates in form and language, even though it is the object of the act of interpretation, which is the task of the mujtahid. (Meaning: 'on the many meanings'? 'The form': i.e., that which comes to the word by virtue of conjugation, or it is said by virtue of arrangement of letters, vowels, and sukoons. (al-Qamar). 'And although it includes etc.': for 'lugha' is the placed word. (al-Qamar). 'Metonym etc.': because the substance, i.e., the essence of letters as they are, does not exist as placed for something; rather it is placed only on condition of association with the form, whether it be a partial form like that of 'rajul', or a general form like that of 'daraba'. So both are observed in the placement. (al-Qamar). 'More relation etc.': for the distinction between 'ar-rajul' and 'ar-rijal' that the first is specific and the second is general is established by the form, not by the substance, for their substance is one. And what is said that the purpose of speech is to make the listener understand, and the listener does not understand without the form, so in that there is only evidence that the form has a role in understanding, not that generality and specificity have more relation to the form. So reflect. (al-Qamar). 'And they': i.e., the aspects of wording; and there is no need for what is in 'Musir' or 'ad-da'ir' of a pronoun referring to the first, and the femininity is due to the predicate. (al-Qamar). 'On individualness': i.e., regardless of whether it has individuals in external reality or not; and the general is excluded by this, for it encompasses individuals as will come. (al-Qamar). 'So the interpreted etc.': an objection against the author's making the interpreted a counterpart to the shared. (al-Qamar). 'It is only among the divisions etc.': and from here you realize that the interpreted is a division of wording in form and language; for if a division of a division is a division, how? And how is it that the word 'sharing' like 'qur'' before interpretation indicates one of the two meanings by placement, and after interpretation that placement indication has not changed, but rather it becomes specific, like menstruation (hayd) for us and purity (tuhr) for al-Shafi'i. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the beginning of the section on 'al-Kitab' (the Book) in a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author is explaining the first division of the subject matter of usul al-fiqh, which concerns the classification of words (alfaz) from the perspective of their linguistic placement (wad') for meanings. The commentator clarifies that the division into four types (khass, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal) is based on induction (istiqra') from the language, not on pure rational enumeration. He also explains that the term 'wujuh' (aspects) used by the original author does not mean 'proofs' but rather 'ways' or 'types', pointing to the fact that usul al-fiqh categorizes words themselves, not proofs. The main point is that when a word is considered from the angle of its original placement for meaning, it can indicate either a single meaning or more than one. If it indicates a single meaning, it is either a specific word (khass) if it denotes an individual without sharing, or a general word ('amm) if it denotes a class including many individuals. If it indicates more than one meaning, then if one of those meanings is made preponderant by interpretation (ta'wil), it is called mu'awwal (interpreted), otherwise it is simply mushtarak (shared, ambiguous). The commentator notes that mu'awwal is actually a subtype of mushtarak, since both are words with multiple meanings, but mu'awwal is one where the mujtahid has chosen a specific meaning based on evidence. This classification is fundamental for understanding how legal rules are derived from texts: the specific applies directly, the general includes all individuals, the shared requires further clarification, and the interpreted requires exegetical effort. The Hanafi school emphasizes the importance of form (sigha) because distinctions like 'man' (who) and 'alladhina' (those who) are made by form, not by the root letters. This passage sets the stage for the detailed discussions of 'amm and khass in later sections.

Key Terms
الخاص (al-khass): A word that indicates a single meaning with individualness (الانفراد) relative to individuals, regardless of whether it has actual individuals in the external world.
العام (al-'amm): A word that indicates a single meaning but with sharing (الاشتراك) among individuals, i.e., it encompasses all individuals of a category.
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word that indicates two or more meanings without one being preponderant by virtue of the original placement. It only signifies all possibilities equally until context or evidence removes ambiguity.
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): A word that indicates multiple meanings but one of them is made preponderant (ترجيح) through interpretation (تأويل) by a mujtahid. It is considered a subdivision of mushtarak in reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about mu'awwal?
A) It is a word that indicates a single meaning with individualness.
B) It is a word that indicates a single meaning with sharing among individuals.
C) It is a word that indicates multiple meanings with no preponderance.
D) It is a word that indicates multiple meanings and is actually a subdivision of mushtarak.

Key Takeaway
The first division of words in Hanafi usul al-fiqh classifies them as khass, 'amm, mushtarak, or mu'awwal, with mu'awwal being a subtype of mushtarak.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Mu'awwal: A Subtype of Mushtarak
Clarifying that mu'awwal is a subtype of mushtarak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why mu'awwal is considered a subtype of mushtarak rather than a separate category, and apply this understanding to resolve textual ambiguity.

Core Idea
Mu'awwal is not a separate type but a mushtarak word after a mujtahid's interpretation.

A common pitfall in studying usul al-fiqh is treating mu'awwal (interpreted) as an independent word category. However, the commentary in this passage clarifies that mu'awwal is in reality a subset of mushtarak (shared/ambiguous). This refined understanding is essential for correctly applying the rules of interpretation, as it reminds us that the original ambiguity of the word remains, and interpretation does not change the word's placement but rather selects one meaning based on evidence.

Guided Path
1
Recall the basis of mushtarak
A word is mushtarak if it is placed for more than one meaning without any preponderance in the original linguistic convention. Examples: 'qur'' (menstruation or purity), 'ayn (eye, spring, spy, etc.)
2
Understand the role of ta'wil (interpretation)
Ta'wil is the act of a mujtahid preferring one of the possible meanings based on contextual or textual evidence. It does not create a new meaning or change the original placement; it merely selects one existing meaning as the intended one for a specific instance.
3
Realize the relationship
After ta'wil, the word is called mu'awwal. However, its original classification as mushtarak remains intact. The commentator explicitly states that mu'awwal 'in reality is only one of the divisions of mushtarak'.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Take the word 'qur''. It is mushtarak between hayd (menstruation) and tuhr (purity). The Hanafi school, through ta'wil, interprets it as hayd; the Shafi'i school interprets it as tuhr. Both interpretations are acts of ta'wil, and the word remains mushtarak in its wad'. It does not become a new type; it becomes mu'awwal for each school.

(السنبلي)
التقسيم الأول باعتبار وضع اللفظ للمعنى
والصيغة هي الهيأة، واللغة وإن كان يشمل المادة والهيأة كليهما لكن أريد بها ههنا: المادة؛ للمقابلة فهما من حيث المجموع كناية عن الوضع فكأنه قال: الأول في أنواع النظم من حيث أي بين الصيغة واللغة المعنى الوضع أي من حيث أنه وضع لمعنى واحد أو أكثر مع قطع النظر عن استعماله وظهوره، وإنما قدم الصيغة على اللغة؛ لأن للعموم والخصوص زيادة تعلق بالصيغة في الأغلب. وهي أربعة الخاص والعام والمشترك والمؤول؛ لأن اللفظ إمّا أن يدل على معنى واحد أو أكثر، فإن كان الأول : فإما أن يدل على الانفراد عن الأفراد فهو الخاص، أو أن يدل مع الاشتراك بين الأفراد فهو العام، وإن كان الثاني : فإما أن يترجح أحد معانيه أي الدلالة على أكثر بالوضع بالتأويل فهو المؤول، وإلا فهو المشترك، فالمؤول في الحقيقة إنما هو من أقسام المشترك الذي دل صيغةً ولغةً وإن كان مفعول فعل التأويل الذي من شأن المجتهد. أي على المعنى الكثيرة الهيأة أي الحاصلة للفظ باعتبار التصرف وقيل باعتبار ترتيب الحروف والحركات والسكنات. (القمر) وإن كان يشمل إلخ فإن اللغة هو اللفظ الموضوع. (القمر) كناية إلخ لأن المادة أي جوهر الحروف من حيث هي هي لم توجد موضوعة لشيء، وإنما وضعت بشرط الاقتران بالهيأة جزئيةً كانت كهيأة رجل، أو كليّةً كهيأة ضرب فيلاحظ كلاهما في الوضع. (القمر) زيادة تعلق إلخ فإن التفرقة بين الرجل والرجال بأن الأول خاص، والثاني عام ثبتت بالصيغة، لا بالمادة، فإن مادتهما واحدة وما قيل من أن المقصود من الكلام إفهام السامع، والسَّامع لا يفهم بدون الصيغة، ففيه أن هذا إنما يدل على أن للصيغة دخلا في الإفهام لا على أن للعموم والخصوص زيادة تعلق بالصيغة فتأمل. (القمر) وهي: أي وجوه النظم ولا حاجة إلى ما في "مسير "الدائر" من الضمير راجع إلى الأول والتأنيث باعتبار الخبر.(القمر) على الانفراد أي مع قطع النظر عن أن يكون له في الخارج أفراد أو لم يكن، وخرج به العام، فإنه يتناول أفرادا على ما سيجيء . (القمر) فالمؤول إلخ إيراد على جعل المصنف المؤول قسيما للمشترك. (القمر) إنما هو من أقسام إلخ: ومن ههنا تتفطن أن المؤول قسم من النظم صيغةً ولغةً، فإن قسم القسم قسم، كيف وأن لفظ المشترك كالقرء قبل التأويل يدل على أحد المعنيين بالوضع، وبعد التأويل لم يتغير تلك الدلالة الوضعية بل يتعين كالحيض عندنا والطهر عند الشافعي (القمر)
Section on the Book (Mabahith al-Kitab): The First Division: Considering the placement of the word for the meaning. And he said: 'their divisions' and did not say 'its divisions' as a hint that the origin of the division is the wording (nazm) and the meaning together. Some say the first three divisions are for the wording and the fourth for the meaning; some say that indication (dalala) and implication (iqtida') are for the meaning and the rest for the wording; and the correct view is that in every division, the wording is considered along with its indication of the meaning. And those are four: meaning what was mentioned previously, i.e., the divisions are four, and under each division are numerous subdivisions as will come. That is because the research is either about the meaning, which is the fourth division, or about the word. If about the word, then either according to its usage, which is the third division, or according to its indication; if in that indication both clarity and hiddenness are considered, then it is the second division; otherwise it is the first division. The first division: considering the placement of the word for the meaning. The first regarding the aspects of wording (nazm): form (sigha) and language (lugha). Meaning that the first division concerns the ways of wording from the perspective of form and language; and the ways are the types and kinds, i.e., the divisions. 'Wording and meaning together': he intended the wording that indicates the meaning, based on the context of his subsequent statement 'and the correct view etc.' (al-Qamar). 'That indication and implication etc.': for if the one seeking proof does not use the wording but rather the meaning, then if the meaning is understood from it linguistically, it is 'indication of the text' (dalalat al-nass); otherwise, if the validity of the wording depends on it legally or rationally, it is 'implication of the text' (iqtida' al-nass). (al-Qamar). 'Is considered etc.': taking the result and inclining toward precision. (al-Qamar). 'Meaning what was mentioned etc.': a clarification of the referent, to repel the misunderstanding that the pronoun refers to a masculine singular, whereas the referent here is 'al-taqsimat' which is a feminine plural. (al-Qamar). 'Four divisions': insinuating that the tanwin in the author's statement 'four' substitutes for the annexed noun. Then know that this enumeration is by induction (istiqra'), not rational (aqlan) revolving between negation and affirmation. (al-Qamar). 'And that etc.': a reason for precision in the four. (al-Qamar). 'Its usage': i.e., in the meaning for which it was placed or other than that. (al-Qamar). 'In it clarity etc.': i.e., in the indication: clarity of the meaning and its hiddenness. (al-Qamar). 'In the ways of wording etc.': this answers a hypothetical objection: that the apparent meaning of 'wujuh' is 'proofs', because it is a plural of 'wajh', and the meaning of 'wajh' in common usage is 'proof', and nothing is mentioned in this division about proof of wording and meaning. So he replied: 'wujuh' here is in the sense of 'ways', because 'wajh' in 'wajh of a thing' means its way; hence the face is called 'wajh' because it is a way to recognize its owner. What is meant by 'wujuh' are the divisions and types. (al-Sunbuli). The first division: considering the placement of the word for the meaning. And 'sigha' (form) is the form (hay'a), and 'lugha' (language) although it includes both the substance (madda) and the form, here what is intended is the substance, for the sake of contrast. So, collectively, they are a metonym for 'placement' (wad'). So it is as if he said: the first is regarding the types of wording from the perspective of placement, i.e., that it is placed for one meaning or more, regardless of its usage and clarity. And he presented 'sigha' over 'lugha' because generality and specificity are more related to form in most cases. And they are four: the specific (al-khass), the general (al-'amm), the shared (al-mushtarak), and the interpreted (al-mu'awwal). Because the word either indicates one meaning or more. If the first: then either it indicates individualness relative to individuals, so it is specific; or it indicates with sharing among individuals, so it is general. If the second: then either one of its meanings is preponderant by placement through interpretation, so it is interpreted; otherwise, it is shared. So the interpreted in reality is only one of the divisions of the shared word, which indicates in form and language, even though it is the object of the act of interpretation, which is the task of the mujtahid. (Meaning: 'on the many meanings'? 'The form': i.e., that which comes to the word by virtue of conjugation, or it is said by virtue of arrangement of letters, vowels, and sukoons. (al-Qamar). 'And although it includes etc.': for 'lugha' is the placed word. (al-Qamar). 'Metonym etc.': because the substance, i.e., the essence of letters as they are, does not exist as placed for something; rather it is placed only on condition of association with the form, whether it be a partial form like that of 'rajul', or a general form like that of 'daraba'. So both are observed in the placement. (al-Qamar). 'More relation etc.': for the distinction between 'ar-rajul' and 'ar-rijal' that the first is specific and the second is general is established by the form, not by the substance, for their substance is one. And what is said that the purpose of speech is to make the listener understand, and the listener does not understand without the form, so in that there is only evidence that the form has a role in understanding, not that generality and specificity have more relation to the form. So reflect. (al-Qamar). 'And they': i.e., the aspects of wording; and there is no need for what is in 'Musir' or 'ad-da'ir' of a pronoun referring to the first, and the femininity is due to the predicate. (al-Qamar). 'On individualness': i.e., regardless of whether it has individuals in external reality or not; and the general is excluded by this, for it encompasses individuals as will come. (al-Qamar). 'So the interpreted etc.': an objection against the author's making the interpreted a counterpart to the shared. (al-Qamar). 'It is only among the divisions etc.': and from here you realize that the interpreted is a division of wording in form and language; for if a division of a division is a division, how? And how is it that the word 'sharing' like 'qur'' before interpretation indicates one of the two meanings by placement, and after interpretation that placement indication has not changed, but rather it becomes specific, like menstruation (hayd) for us and purity (tuhr) for al-Shafi'i. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the beginning of the section on 'al-Kitab' (the Book) in a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author is explaining the first division of the subject matter of usul al-fiqh, which concerns the classification of words (alfaz) from the perspective of their linguistic placement (wad') for meanings. The commentator clarifies that the division into four types (khass, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal) is based on induction (istiqra') from the language, not on pure rational enumeration. He also explains that the term 'wujuh' (aspects) used by the original author does not mean 'proofs' but rather 'ways' or 'types', pointing to the fact that usul al-fiqh categorizes words themselves, not proofs. The main point is that when a word is considered from the angle of its original placement for meaning, it can indicate either a single meaning or more than one. If it indicates a single meaning, it is either a specific word (khass) if it denotes an individual without sharing, or a general word ('amm) if it denotes a class including many individuals. If it indicates more than one meaning, then if one of those meanings is made preponderant by interpretation (ta'wil), it is called mu'awwal (interpreted), otherwise it is simply mushtarak (shared, ambiguous). The commentator notes that mu'awwal is actually a subtype of mushtarak, since both are words with multiple meanings, but mu'awwal is one where the mujtahid has chosen a specific meaning based on evidence. This classification is fundamental for understanding how legal rules are derived from texts: the specific applies directly, the general includes all individuals, the shared requires further clarification, and the interpreted requires exegetical effort. The Hanafi school emphasizes the importance of form (sigha) because distinctions like 'man' (who) and 'alladhina' (those who) are made by form, not by the root letters. This passage sets the stage for the detailed discussions of 'amm and khass in later sections.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word placed for multiple meanings with no preponderance.
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): A mushtarak word after one meaning is preferred by interpretation.
التأويل (al-ta'wil): The act of preferring one meaning of a mushtarak word based on evidence, performed by a mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the commentator's view on mu'awwal?
A) It is a separate category equal to khass and 'amm.
B) It is a subtype of 'amm.
C) It is a subtype of mushtarak.
D) It is not a valid category in usul al-fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Mu'awwal is not an independent category; it is a mushtarak word that has undergone interpretation, and understanding this clarifies the interpretive process.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
First Division of Words: Khas, Aam, Mushtarak, Mu'awwal
Defines four word categories in usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given word as khas, aam, mushtarak, or mu'awwal based on its placement and interpretative evidence.

Core Idea
A word's legal meaning depends on its placement: one-meaning words are specific or general; multi-meaning words are homonym or interpreted.

In the study of usul al-fiqh, words are the building blocks of divine commands. The Hanafi school classifies words based on whether they are placed for one meaning or multiple, and if multiple, whether one meaning is preferred through interpretation. This lesson introduces the foundational taxonomy: khas (specific), aam (general), mushtarak (homonym), and mu'awwal (interpreted homonym). Understanding this classification is essential for deriving rulings from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the number of meanings the word is placed for
Ask: Was the word originally coined for one meaning or more than one? This is the first branch in the classification tree.
Ignore context; focus on the original linguistic placement (wad').
2
If one meaning: distinguish between khas and aam
If the word indicates a single meaning, check whether it singles out an individual (khas) or includes all individuals of that category (aam). The distinction is often made by the word's form (sigha), not its material (lugha).
Example: 'rajul' is khas; 'rijal' is aam.
3
If multiple meanings: distinguish between mushtarak and mu'awwal
If the word has more than one meaning by placement, see if one meaning is made preponderant by evidence (qarina) through ta'wil. If yes, it is mu'awwal; if no, it remains mushtarak.
Mu'awwal is actually a subcategory of mushtarak.
4
Apply to the example of 'qar'
The word 'qar'' has two possible meanings: menstruation (hayd) and purity (tahr). It is mushtarak. Through ta'wil, Hanafis prefer hayd, Shafi'is prefer tahr. Thus it becomes mu'awwal for each school.
The interpretation is the work of the mujtahid.

Section of the Book. First Division: Considering the placing of the word for meaning. And the form (sigha) is the shape, and the language (lugha) although it includes both the material and the shape, but here it is intended: the material; for the sake of contrast, so both together are a metaphor for the placement, as if he said: the first is about the types of expression in terms of the meaning. The placement, i.e., in terms of it being placed for one meaning or more, disregarding its usage and clarity. He gave precedence to form over language because generality and specificity are more related to form in most cases. They are four: the specific (khas), the general (aam), the homonym (mushtarak), and the interpreted (mu'awwal). For the word either indicates one meaning or more. If the former: either it indicates singling out individuals, so it is specific; or it indicates with inclusiveness among individuals, so it is general. If the latter: either one of its meanings is preponderant through interpretation, so it is interpreted; otherwise it is homonym. So in reality the interpreted is a division of the homonym, which indicates by form and language, although it is the object of the act of interpretation which is the task of the mujtahid. (Commentary) The shape: i.e., the shape that occurs to the word by virtue of conjugation, or it is said by virtue of the order of letters, vowels, and sukoons. (al-Qamar) And even though it includes etc., for the language is the placed word. (al-Qamar) Metaphor etc., because the material, i.e., the essence of letters as they are, does not exist placed for anything; rather it is placed conditionally with connection to the shape, whether partial like the shape of 'rajul', or universal like the shape of 'daraba', so both are considered in the placement. (al-Qamar) Increased relation etc., for the distinction between 'rajul' and 'rijal' – that the first is specific and the second is general – is established by the form, not the material, for their material is one. And what is said that the purpose of speech is to inform the listener, and the listener does not understand without the form, so in that is that this only indicates that the form has a role in understanding, not that generality and specificity have increased relation to form, so reflect. (al-Qamar) And they are: i.e., the aspects of expression, and there is no need for what is in 'Misr al-Da'ir' of the pronoun referring to the first and the femininity considering the predicate. (al-Qamar) On singling out: i.e., regardless of whether it has individuals externally or not, and by it the general is excluded, for it includes individuals as will come. (al-Qamar) So the interpreted etc. is an objection to the author making the interpreted a counterpart to the homonym. (al-Qamar) It is only a division etc.: And from here you perceive that the interpreted is a division of expression by form and language, for the division of a division is a division. How? For the word homonym like 'qar'' before interpretation indicates one of the two meanings by placement, and after interpretation that placed indication does not change but becomes determined, like menstruation in our school and purity according to al-Shafi'i. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage opens the first division of words in usul al-fiqh, as explained in the commentary on Noor al-Anwar. The author defines four categories based on whether the word is placed for one meaning or multiple. If one meaning, it is either khas (specific) if it excludes other individuals, or aam (general) if it includes all individuals. If multiple meanings, if one meaning is preponderant through ta'wil (interpretation) it is mu'awwal, otherwise it is mushtarak (homonym). The commentary clarifies that mu'awwal is actually a subdivision of mushtarak, because both have multiple meanings by placement; the difference is that mu'awwal has one meaning preferred by evidence. The famous example of 'qar'' (القرء) is given: in the Hanafi school it is interpreted as hayd (menstruation), while the Shafi'i school interprets it as tahr (purity). This illustrates how a mujtahid's ta'wil can determine the meaning of a homonym. The passage also explains that the terms 'sigha' (form) and 'lugha' (language) together indicate the placement, and that form is more relevant to generality and specificity.

Key Terms
الخاص (al-khass): اللفظ الدال على معنى واحد يدل على الانفراد عن الأفراد
العام (al-aam): اللفظ الدال على معنى واحد مع الاشتراك بين الأفراد
المشترك (al-mushtarak): اللفظ الدال على أكثر من معنى بالوضع ولا ترجيح
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): اللفظ الدال على أكثر من معنى يترجح أحدها بالتأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification of words, which of the following is true about the term 'qar' (القرء)?
A) It is khas (specific) because it refers to a single meaning.
B) It is aam (general) because it includes all times.
C) It is mushtarak (homonym) that is interpreted as hayd by Hanafis.
D) It is mu'awwal because it originally had multiple meanings and no interpretation is possible.

Key Takeaway
Words in usul are classified by their placement: khas and aam for single meanings; mushtarak and mu'awwal for multiple meanings, with mu'awwal being a subset of mushtarak after interpretation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Four Types of Istidlal: 'Ibarah, Isharah, Dalalah, Iqtida'
Explains the four types of istidlal from a text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of textual inference and correctly classify a given derivation example into one of the four categories.

Core Idea
Four types of inference from a text: direct, indirect, implied, and necessary.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding how rulings are derived from Quran and Hadith requires mastery of the modes of inference. This lesson introduces the foundational classification of istidlal into four types based on the relationship between the wording and the intended meaning. By learning these types, you will be able to analyze any textual evidence and determine the strength of the derived ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the inferrer's perspective
The passage explains that the inferrer first looks at meaning, not wording. Understand that a ruling is established by meaning, but meaning is understood from wording.
2
Distinguish when the wording is directly intended
If the wording is driven (masuq) for that meaning, it is 'ibarah al-nass. If not, it is isharah al-nass.
'Ibarah is the direct expression; isharah is indirect indication.
3
Distinguish inference from meaning vs wording
If the inference is not from the wording but from the meaning, check if the meaning is linguistically understood from the text. If yes, it is dalalah al-nass.
Dalalah is implication based on linguistic convention.
4
Determine necessity for the text's validity
If the inferred meaning is necessary for the validity of the text (shar'an or 'aqlan), it is iqtida' al-nass. Otherwise, the inference is corrupt.
Iqtida' is requirement: the text depends on that unstated meaning.
5
Apply the classification to a Quranic example
Use the verse 'Kill the polytheists' (9:5). The literal command to kill is not the intended ruling; the ruling is about killing in battle. This illustrates inference by dalalah (implication) rather than 'ibarah.
The ruling is based on the meaning, not the wording.

الاستدلالات الفاسدة على ما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى.
التقسيم الخامس المشتمل على التقسيمات الأربعة السابقة]
وبعد معرفة هذه الأقسام قسم خامس يشمل الكل أي بعد معرفة هذه الأقسام العشرين التقسيمات الأربعة تقسيم خامس يشمل كلاً من العشرين.
الحاصلة من
=
كونه صفة للفظ بواسطة المعنى، إن نظر المستدل إنما هو إلى المعنى أولاً بالذات دون النظم واللفظ؛ إذ الحكم إنما يثبت بالمعنى دون اللفظ، فإن إباحة قتل المشركين مثلاً يثبت بالمعنى الثابت بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ (التوبة: ٥) إلا أن المعنى مفهوم من اللفظ، فبهذه الجهة هو صفة للفظ أيضًا فافهم. (السنبلي) يؤول إلى حال المعنى: وهو الثابت بعبارة النص، والثابت بإشارة النص، والثابت بدلالة النص، والثابت باقتضاء النص. (القمر) وبواسطته إلخ أي بواسطة المعنى يؤول إلى حال اللفظ، وهو الدال بعبارة النص، والدال بإشارة
النص، والدال بدلالة النص، والدال باقتضاء النص. (القمر) ولذا أي للأول إلى اللفظ بواسطة المعنى. (القمر) الاستدلال إلخ هو انتقال الذهن من الأثر إلى المؤثر كالدخان مع النار ، فإذا أدرك الدخان انتقل منه الذهن إلى النار، وقيل: بالعكس وهو المراد ههنا. (السنبلي) بعبارة النص والمراد من النص ههنا اللفظ الدال على المعنى لا النص المقابل للظاهر كذا في مشكاة الأنوار (القمر) وإلا إلخ : أي وإن لم يكن النظم مسوقا لذلك المراد فهذه الدلالة إشارة النص، وهذه الدلالة لا تكون مقصودةً كما سيجيء. (القمر) صحة النظم: أي صحة المدلول المطابقي للنظم. (القمر) وإن لم يتوقف أي صحة المدلول المطابقي للنظم على ذلك المعنى. (القمر) تقسیم خامس إيماء إلى أن مراد المصنف من القسم التقسيم كيف وليس ههنا قسم واحد يشمل كل الأقسام المذكور بل ههنا تقسيم خامس يشمل أقسامه كلاً من الأقسام المذكورة. (القمر)

التقسيم الخامس المشتمل للتقسيمات.
وهو أربعة أيضًا معرفة مواضعها ومعانيها وترتيبها وأحكامها أي هذا التقسيم أربعة أقسام أيضا معرفة مواضعها أي مأخذ اشتقاق هذه الأقسام، وهو أن لفظ الخاص مشتق من الخصوص: وهو الانفراد، وأن العام مشتق من العموم وهو الشمول، وقس عليه،
ومعانيها: المفهومات الاصطلاحية وهي أن الخاص في الاصطلاح: لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم
أي
على الانفراد، والعام هو ما انتظم جمعا من المسميات. وترتيبها: أي معرفة أن أيها أي الأفراد
يقدَّم
عند التعارض مثلاً إذا تعارض النص والظاهر يقدم النص على الظاهر. وأحكامها أي أن أيها ،قطعي وأيها ظني وأيها واجب التوقف، فالخاص قطعي، والعام المخصوص ظني والمتشابه واجب التوقف.
فإذا ضُربت هذه الأقسام في العشرين تصير الأقسام ثمانين والتقسيمات خمسة، وهذا التقسيم
=
تقسيم خامس :إلخ قلت وجه الحصر فيه بأن يقال: إن معرفة الخاص مثلا إما معرفة معناه اللغوي، أو معرفة معناه الاصطلاحي، أو معرفة حكمه، أو معرفة مقدار قوته عند التعارض وعلى هذا القياس الأقسام الباقية من العام والمشترك والمؤول وغيرها. (السنبلي مواضعها إنما سمي هذه المعنى اللغوية بالمواضع؛ لأنها مأخذ
الاصطلاحية تناسبًا. (القمر) وقس عليه كما أن المشترك مأخوذ من الاشتراك. (القمر)
ومعانيها : معطوف على قوله مواضعها وكذا قوله الآتي وترتيبها وقوله الآتي وأحكامها (القمر) أحكامها إلخ المراد بها الآثار الثابتة بها نحو ثبوت الحكم بها قطعًا أو ظنًا أو وجوب التوقف، فالقول بأن أيها قطعي وأيها ظني بمجاز؛ لأن الأقسام نفسها لا تكون قطعيًا وظنيا ،حقيقة، بل الحكم الثابت منها يكون كذلك، ولو ذكر ترتيبها آخرًا لكان أحسن؛ لأن مدار الترتيب الموضوع على كون الأقسام قطعيًا وظنيا، فلابد من ذكر القطع والظن مقدما فافهم. (السنبلي) تصير الأقسام ثمانين: هذا على سبيل التجوز، والأصل: أن الأقسام عشرون، ومعرفة كل قسم تنقسم إلى أربع معرفات، فيحصل ثمانون معرفة لا ثمانون قسمًا. (القمر) وهذا التقسيم إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن بهذا التقسيم الخامس زاد عدد الأقسام على العشرين، فبطل الحصر فيها، فأجاب بما :حاصله أن الحصر المذكور في العشرين كان لأقسام ،القرآن وهذا التقسيم في الواقع ليس تقسيما للقرآن بل لأسامي أقسام القرآن وإن كان قول الشارح: بل لأسامي أقسام القرآن مبنيا على التسامح من حيث أن هذا التقسيم في الحقيقة ليس تقسيماً لأسامي أقسام القرآن أيضًا، بل مورد هذا التقسيم في الحقيقة هو =
The fifth classification encompassing the divisions. It leads to the state of the meaning and through it to the wording, hence it was said: This classification is for meaning, not wording. They are also four: inference by the text's expression, by its indication, by its implication, and by its requirement. Because the inferrer: if he infers from the wording, then if it is the intended meaning, it is the text's expression; otherwise, it is the text's indication. If he does not infer from the wording but from the meaning, then if it is understood from it linguistically, it is the text's implication; otherwise, if the validity of the wording (in shari' or reason) depends on it, it is the text's requirement; and if it does not depend on it, it is from the corrupt inferences, as will come later, God willing. The fifth classification encompassing the previous four classifications. After knowing these divisions, there is a fifth division that includes everything, i.e., after knowing these twenty divisions, there are four classifications: a fifth division that includes each of the twenty. Resulting from: it being a description of the wording through the meaning; indeed the look of the inferrer is first and primarily to the meaning, not the wording or utterance, because the ruling is established by the meaning, not the wording. For example, the permissibility of killing polytheists is established by the meaning established by His statement: 'Kill the polytheists' (9:5), except that the meaning is understood from the wording, so in this respect it is also a description of the wording, so understand. (al-Sunbuli) It leads to the state of the meaning: which is established by the text's expression, established by the text's indication, established by the text's implication, and established by the text's requirement. (al-Qamar) And through it etc., i.e., through the meaning it leads to the state of the wording, which is the indicator by the text's expression, indicator by the text's indication, indicator by the text's implication, indicator by the text's requirement. (al-Qamar) Hence i.e., because of the first, to the wording through the meaning. (al-Qamar) Inference etc. is the transition of the mind from the effect to the cause, like smoke with fire; when one perceives smoke, the mind transitions from it to the fire. And it was said: the opposite, and that is what is meant here. (al-Sunbuli) By the text's expression: what is meant by 'text' here is the wording indicating the meaning, not 'text' as opposed to 'apparent', as in Mishkat al-Anwar. (al-Qamar) Otherwise etc., i.e., if the wording is not intended for that meaning, then this indication is the text's indication, and this indication is not intended, as will come. (al-Qamar) Validity of the wording: i.e., validity of the literal signification of the wording. (al-Qamar) And if it does not depend i.e., the validity of the literal signification of the wording does not depend on that meaning. (al-Qamar) A fifth classification: an allusion that the author's intent from 'division' is 'classification'; how could there be a single division that includes all the mentioned divisions? Rather, there is a fifth classification that includes its divisions, each of the mentioned divisions. (al-Qamar) The fifth classification encompassing the classifications. It is also four: knowledge of their derivations, their meanings, their order, and their rulings; i.e., this classification is also four divisions: knowledge of their derivations i.e., the source of derivation of these divisions, like the word 'specific' is derived from 'specificity': it is exclusivity, and 'general' is derived from 'generality': it is inclusiveness, and analogize to it. And their meanings: the conventional concepts; that 'specific' in terminology is a word placed for a known meaning individually, and 'general' is what comprises a collection of names. And their order: i.e., knowing which one is given precedence when conflicting; for example, if text and apparent conflict, text is given precedence over apparent. And their rulings: i.e., which is definitive, which is presumptive, and which requires suspension; so the specific is definitive, the general that has been specified is presumptive, and the ambiguous requires suspension. So if these divisions are multiplied by the twenty, the divisions become eighty, and the classifications are five. This classification: a fifth classification. I say: the justification for the restriction is that knowledge of the specific, for example, is either knowledge of its linguistic meaning, or knowledge of its conventional meaning, or knowledge of its ruling, or knowledge of the extent of its strength when conflicting. And analogize to this the remaining divisions of general, shared, interpreted, etc. (al-Sunbuli) Their derivations: these linguistic meanings are called 'derivations' because they are the source of the conventional terms, as a correspondence. (al-Qamar) And analogize to it like 'shared' is taken from 'sharing'. (al-Qamar) And their meanings: connected to his statement 'their derivations', and likewise his statement later 'their order', and his statement later 'their rulings'. (al-Qamar) Their rulings etc.: what is meant by them are the effects established by them, like the establishment of a ruling by them definitively or presumptively or the obligation of suspension. So saying 'which is definitive and which is presumptive' is a metaphor because the divisions themselves are not in reality definitive or presumptive; rather, the ruling established from them is so. And had he mentioned their order later, it would have been better because the basis of order is built on the divisions being definitive or presumptive, so it is necessary to mention definitiveness and presumptiveness first. (al-Sunbuli) The divisions become eighty: this is metaphorical; the principle is that the divisions are twenty, and knowledge of each division is divided into four cognitions, so eighty cognitions are obtained, not eighty divisions. (al-Qamar) And this classification etc.: it repels an estimated objection: that by this fifth classification, the number of divisions increased beyond twenty, so the restriction to them is invalid. So he answered by saying that the restriction mentioned in the twenty was for the divisions of the Quran, and this classification is in reality not a division of the Quran but of the names of the Quran's divisions, although the commentator's statement 'but of the names of the Quran's divisions' is based on tolerance, since this classification in reality is not a division of the names of the Quran's divisions either, rather the subject of this classification in reality is...
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains two key aspects of the fifth classification in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. First, it discusses the four types of istidlal (inference) from a text: expression (`ibarah), indication (`isharah), implication (dalalah), and requirement (iqtida'). These correspond to how a ruling is derived from the wording: if the wording directly speaks to the ruling, it's `ibarah; if it indirectly points to it, it's `isharah; if the meaning is understood linguistically from the wording without being directly stated, it's dalalah; and if the validity of the wording itself depends on an unstated meaning, it's iqtida'. Any other inference is considered corrupt. The passage then introduces a second aspect: after the twenty divisions of the Quran (e.g., specific, general, etc.), there is a fifth classification that relates to the knowledge of these divisions themselves. This knowledge is broken down into four areas: 1) mawadi' (derivations of the terms), 2) ma'ani (their terminological meanings), 3) tartib (their order and precedence when conflicting), and 4) ahkam (their legal strength: definitive, presumptive, or requiring suspension). When these four aspects are applied to the twenty divisions, the number of knowledge areas becomes eighty. The commentary clarifies that this does not create new divisions of the Quran but rather expands the ways of knowing them.

Key Terms
عبارة النص ('ibarah al-nass): Inference by the direct expression of the text; the text is explicitly intended for that meaning.
إشارة النص (isharah al-nass): Inference by the indication of the text; the text is not directly intended for that meaning but it points to it indirectly.
دلالة النص (dalalah al-nass): Inference by the implication of the text; the meaning is understood linguistically from the text even if not explicitly stated.
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' al-nass): Inference by the requirement of the text; the validity of the text depends on an unstated meaning that is necessary for its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of inference is used when the validity of the text itself (shar'an or 'aqlan) depends on an unstated meaning?
A) 'Ibarah al-nass
B) Isharah al-nass
C) Dalalah al-nass
D) Iqtida' al-nass

Key Takeaway
The four types of istidlal—'ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida'—form the basis of Hanafi textual analysis, categorizing how meanings are derived from scripture.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
7 min
The Four Dimensions of Knowing Quranic Divisions: Mawadi', Ma'ani, Tartib, Ahkam
Introduces the four aspects of knowledge for each Quranic division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four aspects of knowledge related to any Quranic division (such as 'amm, khass) and explain how they multiply the twenty divisions into eighty cognitions.

Core Idea
Knowing a Quranic division requires four dimensions: its etymology, definition, precedence, and legal strength.

After learning the twenty divisions of the Quran (like 'amm, khass, mujmal, etc.), Hanafi usul scholars realized that each division can be known from four angles. This lesson introduces those four aspects: mawadi' (derivations), ma'ani (meanings), tartib (order when conflicting), and ahkam (legal strength). When applied to each division, they yield eighty cognitions, not new divisions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of the fifth classification
This fifth classification is not a new division of the Quran but a meta-classification about how we know the existing twenty divisions.
The passage stresses that it is about the knowledge of the divisions, not the divisions themselves.
2
Identify the four aspects
The four aspects are: 1) mawadi'—the derivational sources of the terms (e.g., 'specific' from 'specificity'), 2) ma'ani—the terminological definitions, 3) tartib—the order of priority when divisions conflict (e.g., text over apparent), 4) ahkam—the legal strength (definitive, presumptive, or requiring suspension).
3
Apply to a specific division
Take the division 'khass' (specific). Mawadi': derived from 'khussus' meaning exclusivity. Ma'ani: defined as a word for a single known meaning. Tartib: it takes precedence over 'amm when conflicting. Ahkam: it is qat'i (definitive).
The passage gives similar for 'amm.
4
Understand the multiplication to eighty
Each of the twenty divisions has these four aspects of knowledge. 20 × 4 = 80 cognitions. The passage clarifies this is metaphorical; the divisions themselves remain twenty.
5
Note the response to an objection
An objection is raised: this fifth classification increases the count beyond twenty. The answer is that the twenty were divisions of the Quran, while this fifth classification is about the names/descriptions of those divisions.
This is a meta-classification.

ومعانيها : معطوف على قوله مواضعها وكذا قوله الآتي وترتيبها وقوله الآتي وأحكامها (القمر) أحكامها إلخ المراد بها الآثار الثابتة بها نحو ثبوت الحكم بها قطعًا أو ظنًا أو وجوب التوقف، فالقول بأن أيها قطعي وأيها ظني بمجاز؛ لأن الأقسام نفسها لا تكون قطعيًا وظنيا ،حقيقة، بل الحكم الثابت منها يكون كذلك، ولو ذكر ترتيبها آخرًا لكان أحسن؛ لأن مدار الترتيب الموضوع على كون الأقسام قطعيًا وظنيا، فلابد من ذكر القطع والظن مقدما فافهم. (السنبلي) تصير الأقسام ثمانين: هذا على سبيل التجوز، والأصل: أن الأقسام عشرون، ومعرفة كل قسم تنقسم إلى أربع معرفات، فيحصل ثمانون معرفة لا ثمانون قسمًا. (القمر) وهذا التقسيم إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن بهذا التقسيم الخامس زاد عدد الأقسام على العشرين، فبطل الحصر فيها، فأجاب بما :حاصله أن الحصر المذكور في العشرين كان لأقسام ،القرآن وهذا التقسيم في الواقع ليس تقسيما للقرآن بل لأسامي أقسام القرآن وإن كان قول الشارح: بل لأسامي أقسام القرآن مبنيا على التسامح من حيث أن هذا التقسيم في الحقيقة ليس تقسيماً لأسامي أقسام القرآن أيضًا، بل مورد هذا التقسيم في الحقيقة هو =
The fifth classification encompassing the divisions. It leads to the state of the meaning and through it to the wording, hence it was said: This classification is for meaning, not wording. They are also four: inference by the text's expression, by its indication, by its implication, and by its requirement. Because the inferrer: if he infers from the wording, then if it is the intended meaning, it is the text's expression; otherwise, it is the text's indication. If he does not infer from the wording but from the meaning, then if it is understood from it linguistically, it is the text's implication; otherwise, if the validity of the wording (in shari' or reason) depends on it, it is the text's requirement; and if it does not depend on it, it is from the corrupt inferences, as will come later, God willing. The fifth classification encompassing the previous four classifications. After knowing these divisions, there is a fifth division that includes everything, i.e., after knowing these twenty divisions, there are four classifications: a fifth division that includes each of the twenty. Resulting from: it being a description of the wording through the meaning; indeed the look of the inferrer is first and primarily to the meaning, not the wording or utterance, because the ruling is established by the meaning, not the wording. For example, the permissibility of killing polytheists is established by the meaning established by His statement: 'Kill the polytheists' (9:5), except that the meaning is understood from the wording, so in this respect it is also a description of the wording, so understand. (al-Sunbuli) It leads to the state of the meaning: which is established by the text's expression, established by the text's indication, established by the text's implication, and established by the text's requirement. (al-Qamar) And through it etc., i.e., through the meaning it leads to the state of the wording, which is the indicator by the text's expression, indicator by the text's indication, indicator by the text's implication, indicator by the text's requirement. (al-Qamar) Hence i.e., because of the first, to the wording through the meaning. (al-Qamar) Inference etc. is the transition of the mind from the effect to the cause, like smoke with fire; when one perceives smoke, the mind transitions from it to the fire. And it was said: the opposite, and that is what is meant here. (al-Sunbuli) By the text's expression: what is meant by 'text' here is the wording indicating the meaning, not 'text' as opposed to 'apparent', as in Mishkat al-Anwar. (al-Qamar) Otherwise etc., i.e., if the wording is not intended for that meaning, then this indication is the text's indication, and this indication is not intended, as will come. (al-Qamar) Validity of the wording: i.e., validity of the literal signification of the wording. (al-Qamar) And if it does not depend i.e., the validity of the literal signification of the wording does not depend on that meaning. (al-Qamar) A fifth classification: an allusion that the author's intent from 'division' is 'classification'; how could there be a single division that includes all the mentioned divisions? Rather, there is a fifth classification that includes its divisions, each of the mentioned divisions. (al-Qamar) The fifth classification encompassing the classifications. It is also four: knowledge of their derivations, their meanings, their order, and their rulings; i.e., this classification is also four divisions: knowledge of their derivations i.e., the source of derivation of these divisions, like the word 'specific' is derived from 'specificity': it is exclusivity, and 'general' is derived from 'generality': it is inclusiveness, and analogize to it. And their meanings: the conventional concepts; that 'specific' in terminology is a word placed for a known meaning individually, and 'general' is what comprises a collection of names. And their order: i.e., knowing which one is given precedence when conflicting; for example, if text and apparent conflict, text is given precedence over apparent. And their rulings: i.e., which is definitive, which is presumptive, and which requires suspension; so the specific is definitive, the general that has been specified is presumptive, and the ambiguous requires suspension. So if these divisions are multiplied by the twenty, the divisions become eighty, and the classifications are five. This classification: a fifth classification. I say: the justification for the restriction is that knowledge of the specific, for example, is either knowledge of its linguistic meaning, or knowledge of its conventional meaning, or knowledge of its ruling, or knowledge of the extent of its strength when conflicting. And analogize to this the remaining divisions of general, shared, interpreted, etc. (al-Sunbuli) Their derivations: these linguistic meanings are called 'derivations' because they are the source of the conventional terms, as a correspondence. (al-Qamar) And analogize to it like 'shared' is taken from 'sharing'. (al-Qamar) And their meanings: connected to his statement 'their derivations', and likewise his statement later 'their order', and his statement later 'their rulings'. (al-Qamar) Their rulings etc.: what is meant by them are the effects established by them, like the establishment of a ruling by them definitively or presumptively or the obligation of suspension. So saying 'which is definitive and which is presumptive' is a metaphor because the divisions themselves are not in reality definitive or presumptive; rather, the ruling established from them is so. And had he mentioned their order later, it would have been better because the basis of order is built on the divisions being definitive or presumptive, so it is necessary to mention definitiveness and presumptiveness first. (al-Sunbuli) The divisions become eighty: this is metaphorical; the principle is that the divisions are twenty, and knowledge of each division is divided into four cognitions, so eighty cognitions are obtained, not eighty divisions. (al-Qamar) And this classification etc.: it repels an estimated objection: that by this fifth classification, the number of divisions increased beyond twenty, so the restriction to them is invalid. So he answered by saying that the restriction mentioned in the twenty was for the divisions of the Quran, and this classification is in reality not a division of the Quran but of the names of the Quran's divisions, although the commentator's statement 'but of the names of the Quran's divisions' is based on tolerance, since this classification in reality is not a division of the names of the Quran's divisions either, rather the subject of this classification in reality is...
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar explains two key aspects of the fifth classification in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. First, it discusses the four types of istidlal (inference) from a text: expression (`ibarah), indication (`isharah), implication (dalalah), and requirement (iqtida'). These correspond to how a ruling is derived from the wording: if the wording directly speaks to the ruling, it's `ibarah; if it indirectly points to it, it's `isharah; if the meaning is understood linguistically from the wording without being directly stated, it's dalalah; and if the validity of the wording itself depends on an unstated meaning, it's iqtida'. Any other inference is considered corrupt. The passage then introduces a second aspect: after the twenty divisions of the Quran (e.g., specific, general, etc.), there is a fifth classification that relates to the knowledge of these divisions themselves. This knowledge is broken down into four areas: 1) mawadi' (derivations of the terms), 2) ma'ani (their terminological meanings), 3) tartib (their order and precedence when conflicting), and 4) ahkam (their legal strength: definitive, presumptive, or requiring suspension). When these four aspects are applied to the twenty divisions, the number of knowledge areas becomes eighty. The commentary clarifies that this does not create new divisions of the Quran but rather expands the ways of knowing them.

Key Terms
مواضع (mawadi'): The derivational sources of the terms (e.g., 'specific' from 'specificity').
ترتيب (tartib): The order of priority when textual divisions conflict (e.g., text over apparent).
أحكام (ahkam): The legal strength of each division (definitive, presumptive, or requiring suspension).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the legal strength (ahkam) of the division 'khass' (specific)?
A) Qat'i (definitive)
B) Zanni (presumptive)
C) Requires tawaqquf (suspension)
D) It is not mentioned

Key Takeaway
Each Quranic division is known through four dimensions: derivation, definition, priority, and legal strength; this meta-knowledge yields eighty cognitions without adding new divisions.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
beginner
8 min
Definition of al-Khas and Its Types
Defining 'al-Khas' and explaining its three divisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-Khas, state its three types, and classify a given word as khas, amm, mushtarak, or muhmal based on the conditions in the definition.

Core Idea
Al-Khas is a word with a specific meaning, excluding muhmal, mushtarak, and amm.

This lesson begins the study of al-Khas (the specific), a foundational term in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The passage from Noorul Anwar provides a precise definition and then categorizes specific words into three types based on their scope: genus, species, or individual. Understanding this definition is crucial for distinguishing specific texts from general ones and for proper legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Deconstruct the definition phrase by phrase
The definition has four parts: (1) every word, (2) placed for a meaning, (3) known, (4) in isolation. Identify what each part contributes to the overall meaning.
The word 'every' ensures comprehensiveness.
2
Identify what each part excludes
For each part, determine which type of word is excluded. Part 2 excludes muhmal; part 3 can exclude mushtarak if interpreted as 'known intended'; part 4 excludes mushtarak and amm.
The commentator explains two interpretations of 'ma'lum'.
3
Learn the three types of al-Khas
Memorize the three divisions: khussus al-jins (genus, differing rulings), khussus al-naw' (species, same ruling), khussus al-ayn (individual, single entity).
The criterion is whether the individuals share rulings or not.
4
Apply the definition to classify words
Given a word, decide if it is khas, amm, mushtarak, or muhmal using the conditions. Then if khas, identify its type.
Examples: 'insaan' (human) is khussus al-naw'; 'shams' (sun) is khussus al-ayn; 'hayawaan' (animal) is khussus al-jins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الخاص فكل لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم على الانفراد. فقوله: "كل لفظ" بمنزلة الجنس لكل ألفاظ والباقي كالفصل. فقوله: "وضع لمعنى" يخرج المهمل. وقوله: "معلوم" إن كان معناه معلوم المراد فيخرج منه المشترك؛ لأنه غير معلوم المراد، وإن كان معناه معلوم البيان لم يخرج المشترك منه، ويخرج من قوله: "على الانفراد"؛ لأن معناه حينئذٍ أن يكون المعنى منفردًا عن الأفراد، وعن معنى آخر، فيخرج عنه المشترك والعام جميعًا. وأما ذكر كلمة "كل" فإنه وإن كان مستنكرًا في التعريفات في اصطلاح المنطق، ولكن القصد ههنا لبيان الاطراد والضبط، وهو إنما يحصل بلفظ "كل". البيان وهو إما أن يكون خصوص الجنس، أو خصوص النوع، أو خصوص العين، خصوص الجنس إن كان اللفظ مشتملاً على كثيرين متفاوتين في أحكام الشرع، أو خصوص النوع: إن كان مشتملاً على كثيرين متفقين في الحكم، أو خصوص العين: إن كان له معنى واحد حقيقة.
As for al-Khas, it is every word placed for a known meaning in isolation. His saying: 'every word' is like a genus for all words, and the rest [of the definition] is like differentiae. His saying: 'placed for a meaning' excludes the meaningless (al-muhmal). His saying: 'known' — if its meaning is 'known in terms of what is intended', then it excludes the ambiguous (al-mushtarak), because it is not known what is intended; if its meaning is 'known in terms of clarification', then the ambiguous is not excluded [by that], and it is excluded by his saying: 'in isolation', because its meaning then is that the meaning is isolated from individuals and from another meaning, so both the ambiguous and the general (al-amm) are excluded. As for the mention of the word 'every', although it is disapproved in definitions in the terminology of logic, but the aim here is to express comprehensiveness and restriction, which is only achieved by the word 'every'. The clarification: it is either particularity of genus, or particularity of species, or particularity of individual. Particularity of genus: if the word includes many [individuals] differing in the rulings of the Sharia; particularity of species: if it includes many agreeing in the ruling; particularity of individual: if it has a single meaning in reality.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage defines the technical term 'al-Khas' (the specific) as used in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It is a definition from the commentary of Noorul Anwar. The commentator begins by quoting the matn: 'As for al-Khas, it is every word placed for a known meaning in isolation.' Then he explains each part. 'Every word' serves as a genus, covering all words, while the remaining conditions (placed for a meaning, known, in isolation) act as differentiae. 'Placed for a meaning' excludes al-muhmal (meaningless or unassigned words), which have no lexical assignment. The word 'known' (ma'lum) is ambiguous: if it means 'known in terms of what is intended' (ma'lum al-murad), it excludes al-mushtarak (homonym/ambiguous word) because a homonym has multiple possible intended meanings. If it means 'known in terms of clarity' (ma'lum al-bayan), then homonyms are not excluded by that clause, but they are excluded by the condition 'in isolation' (ala al-infirad). This phrase implies the meaning is isolated both from other individuals and from another meaning. Thus, the general word (al-amm) is also excluded because it has many individuals. The inclusion of 'every' (kull) is unusual in logical definitions, but here it emphasizes that the definition covers all instances (ittirdad) and excludes everything else (dabt). The passage concludes by explaining three types of al-Khas: (1) Khussus al-jins (particularity of genus): a word that covers many individuals with different Sharia rulings, e.g., 'animal' includes humans, beasts, etc., with different rulings. (2) Khussus al-naw' (particularity of species): a word that covers many individuals agreeing in the same ruling, e.g., 'human' includes all humans who share the same legal obligations. (3) Khussus al-ayn (particularity of individual): a word that has a single real meaning, e.g., 'the sun' or 'Zayd'. Thus, al-Khas is a term that applies to all these categories. This definition is foundational for understanding how specific texts are treated in legal interpretation and for distinguishing them from general (amm) and ambiguous (mushtarak) expressions.

Key Terms
خاص (khaṣṣ): A word placed for a known meaning in isolation, covering particularity of genus, species, or individual.
مهمل (muhmal): A word not placed for any meaning (i.e., without lexical assignment).
مشترك (mushtarak): A homonym: a word with multiple unrelated meanings without contextual preference.
عام (ʿāmm): A word that includes all individuals of its category without restriction.
خصوص الجنس (khuṣūṣ al-jins): A specific word covering many individuals with differing legal rulings across species.
خصوص النوع (khuṣūṣ al-nawʿ): A specific word covering many individuals that share the same legal ruling.
خصوص العين (khuṣūṣ al-ʿayn): A specific word referring to a single individual entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in the passage, which type of al-Khas refers to a word that includes many individuals who all share the same legal ruling?
A) Khussus al-jins (particularity of genus)
B) Khussus al-naw' (particularity of species)
C) Khussus al-ayn (particularity of individual)
D) al-amm (the general)

Key Takeaway
Al-Khas is a word with a specific, known meaning that is isolated from other individuals and meanings; it divides into genus, species, and individual types.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Defining al-Khass: Conditions and Distinctions
Analyzing the precise wording of the definition of al-khass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the definition of al-khass to identify which words qualify as specific and explain why homonyms (mushtarak) and general words ('amm) are excluded.

Core Idea
Al-Khass is a word indicating one meaning individually; it excludes the homonym and the general.

In this lesson, we examine the precise definition of al-khass (the specific) as a foundational term in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. We will dissect its wording, particularly the terms 'known' (ma'lum) and 'individually' ('ala al-infrad), to understand how they exclude other categories like homonyms and general terms. This precision is essential for determining the scope of legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definition
Read the definition: 'lafz yadullu 'ala ma'na wahid 'ala al-infrad'. Identify each component: lafz (word), yadullu (indicates), ma'na wahid (one meaning), 'ala al-infrad (individually).
The definition is from the matn.
2
Analyze the condition 'ma'lum'
The word 'known' can be interpreted in two ways: 'known in what is intended' (ma'lum al-murad) which excludes mushtarak, or 'known in clarity' (ma'lum al-bayan) which does not. Understand both possibilities.
This shows attention to linguistic precision.
3
Apply exclusion of mushtarak and 'amm
The phrase 'ala al-infrad' ensures that the meaning is separate from other meanings (excluding mushtarak) and separate from individuals of a general category (excluding 'amm). Verify by considering 'rajul' (man) which has individual men considered.
The dual (tathniya) is included because it disregards individuals beyond two.
4
Understand the use of 'lafz' vs 'nazm'
The author uses 'lafz' (word) instead of 'nazm' (arrangement) because these divisions apply to all Arabic words, not just Quranic text. 'Nazm' is used later for stylistic elegance.
This reflects the principle of comprehensive applicability.
5
Note the role of 'kull' in definitions
The word 'kull' (every) is included in definitions to express comprehensiveness and precision, even though it is sometimes avoided in logic.
This ensures the definition covers all instances.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث الخاص
تعريف الخاص وأقسامه
وقوله: "معلوم" إن كان معناه معلوم المراد فيخرج منه المشترك؛ لأنه غير معلوم المراد، وإن كان معناه معلوم البيان لم يخرج المشترك منه، ويخرج من قوله: "على الانفراد"؛ لأن معناه حينئذٍ أن يكون المعنى منفردًا عن الأفراد، وعن معنى آخر، فيخرج عنه المشترك والعام جميعًا، وإنما ذكر اللفظ ههنا دون النظم جريا على الأصل، ولأن الظاهر أن هذه الأقسام ليست مختصة بالكتاب، بل يجري في جميع كلمات العرب، وإنما ذكر النظم في التقسيمات رعاية للأدب؛ لأن النظم في الأصل جمع اللؤلؤ في السلك بخلاف اللفظ فإنه في اللغة الرمي، وأما ذكر كلمة "كل" فإنه وإن كان مستنكرًا في التعريفات في اصطلاح المنطق، ولكن القصد ههنا لبيان الاطراد والضبط، وهو إنما يحصل بلفظ " كل ".
البيان
وهو إما أن يكون خصوص الجنس، أو خصوص النوع، أو خصوص العين،
معلوم المراد: أي معلوم ما هو المراد منه . (القمر) لأنه إلخ : أي لأن المشترك موضوع لمعنى غير معلوم المراد.(القمر) معلوم البيان أي معلوم بيانه وظهوره عن اللفظ (القمر) على الانفراد إلى أريد به ما يتناول اللفظ معنى واحدًا مع قطع النظر عن الأفراد فرجال لا انفراد فيه؛ لأن أفراده منظورة (السنبلي) لأن معناه حينئذٍ إلخ إنما قال: حينئذٍ ؛ لأن معنى الانفراد على التقدير الأول، وهو خروج المشترك عن قوله: معلوم الانفراد عن الأفراد فيخرج عنه إلخ لأن المشترك ليس فيه الانفراد عن المعنى الآخر، والعام ليس فيه الانفراد عن الأفراد، فرجال أفراده منظورة ، وأما المثنى فداخل في الخاص؛ لأنه يشمل فردين، ففيه قطع النظر عن الأفراد. (القمر) ليست مختصة إلخ حتى يضطر إلى إيراد النظم رعاية للأدب. (القمر)
