فاقطعوا يده فإن عاد فاقطعوا رجله عن أبي هريرة

(القمر)

بيان اسم الفاعل مثل الأمر لا يحتمل التكرار وكل السرقات لا يعلم إلا في آخر العمر فصار الواحد مرادا بيقين وبالفعل الواحد لا تقطع إلا يد واحدة وأيضا فاقطعوا دال على القطع وهو أيضا لا يحتمل العدد فلا تثبت اليد اليسرى من الآية لا يقال فينبغي أن لا تقطع الرجل اليسرى في الكرة الثانية أيضا لأنا نقول إن الرجل غير متعرضة بها في الآية فلا بأس أن يثبت بنص آخر واليد لما كانت متعرضة بها في الآية وتعين اليمنى مرادا منها لا يجوز أن تثبت اليسرى بخبر الواحد الذي لا تجوز الزيادة به على الكتاب لأنه لم يبق المحل المعين الذي تعين أي اليد اليمنى بالإجماع بخلاف الجلد فإنه كلما يزني غير المحصن يجلد لأن البدن صالح للجلد دائما عن عائشة في شأن لا يعلم إلخ فلو كان المراد كل السرقات لتوقف قطع السارق على آخر الحياة وهو باطل بالإجماع (القمر) وبالفعل إلخ دفع لما يتوهم من قطع اليدين بسرقة واحدة (القمر) فينبغي أن لا تقطع إلخ لأن القطع لا يحتمل العدد (القمر) فلا بأس أن يثبت إلخ هكذا قال غير واحد ويخدشه أن الآية معترضة لليد واليمنى مراد منها على ما سيجيء فكما أن الآية غير متعرضة للرجل اليسرى كذلك غير متعرضة لليد اليسرى فيصح إثبات قطع اليد اليسرى بنص آخر كما صح إثبات قطع الرجل اليسرى بنص آخر فالفرق تحكم والحق أن يقال إن إثبات قطع الرجل اليسرى في المرة الثانية إنما هو بالإجماع كما قال ابن الهمام له (القمر) مرادا منها إلخ أي بدليل الإجماع والسنة القولية والفعلية لما أخرج الجماعة إلا ابن ماجة المخزومية وفيه فأمر النبي بقطع يمينها ولما رواه الدار قطني من حديث صفوان ابن أمية وفيه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قطع يمين السارق من الزند كذا قال العلي القاري وقراءة ابن مسعود له أيمانهما مكان أيديهما (القمر) لأنه لم يبق إلخ دليل لقوله لا يجوز أن تثبت إلخ (القمر) بخلاف الجلد إلخ إشارة إلى دفع ما يتوهم من أن في قوله تعالى الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحد مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَة (النور ٢) يكون الزنا الواحد مرادا بالدليل المذكور في آية السرقة فيجب الجلد مرة مع أنه ليس كذلك إذ لو زنى غير المحصن يجلد ثم لو زنى بعد الجلد ثم وثم وهكذا وحاصل الدفع أن محل الجلد هو البدن وهو باق صالح للجلد دائما فلما يزنى غير المحصن يجلد وهذا من قبيل تكرار السبب عند قبول المحل التكرار بخلاف السرقة فإن محل القطع الذي أريد بالإجماع هي اليد اليمنى فلما قطعت بالسرقة الأولى لم يبق المحل فلا يتأدى التكرار كذا أفيد من بحر العلوم أبي نسبا وعلما نور الله مرقده وإنما قال غير المحصن لأن المحصن يرجم وشرائط إحصان الرجم الحرية والعقل والبلوغ والإسلام والوطء كون الوطء بنكاح صحيح حال الدخول وكونهما بصفة الإحصان المذكورة وقت الوطء فإحصان كل منهما شرط لصيرورة الآخر به محصنا كذا في الدر المختار (القمر)
Section on the Specific (al-Khass). Explanation that the active participle (ism fa’il) like the command does not imply repetition. It is indicated by necessity (iqtida’) like his saying: “You are divorced (anta taliq)” – that is outside what we are in, and its explanation will come. So that by the verse on theft only one theft is intended, and by one act only one hand is cut. Derivation on the non-implication of repetition for the active participle, and an objection to al-Shafi’i regarding his opinion. Its explanation: al-Shafi’i says: The thief’s right hand is cut first, then his left foot second, then his left hand third, then his right foot fourth, due to his (the Prophet’s) saying: “Whoever steals, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut off his foot; if he returns, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut off his foot.” According to us (Hanafis), the left hand is not cut in the third instance; rather he is imprisoned until he repents, because the active participle “al-sariq” (the thief) indicates the source (masdar) linguistically, and the source is only intended as one or the whole. [The whole] is real. It indicates the source by necessity, etc. For “al-taliq” linguistically indicates a divorce that is a description of the woman, not a divorce in the sense of talaq (the act of divorcing), like “al-salam” in the sense of taslim (salutation). The man’s act is the divorcing (tatliq), not the first. For the first is a necessary description that the woman is described by, but “al-taliq” indicates divorcing (tatliq) by necessity, so it is established legally for the validity of this speech, i.e., describing the husband as pronouncing an informative divorce. This is in al-’Inayah. From here is clarified what the commentator said in al-Minhayah: For the divorce understood linguistically in the phrase “you are divorced” is the divorce that is a description of the woman, not the divorcing that is the man’s act. End quote. (al-Qamar) Then it is outside what we are in: For with his saying “you are divorced” only one divorce occurs even if he intends more than that – as in al-Hidayah. (al-Qamar) Then his left foot second: This is by consensus, either from the ankle as ‘Umar did and most scholars followed, or from half the foot at the lace tie as he (the Prophet) did and he leaves for him a heel to walk on – transmitted in some marginalia from Fath al-Qadir. (al-Qamar) “Whoever steals etc.”: Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said: The hadith with this wording is not known. Al-Daraqutni produced it with explanation: The Messenger of Allah said: “If the thief steals, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut off his foot; if he returns, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut off his foot.” There are many various chains to it, none free from criticism. Al-Tahawi said: We followed these reports and did not find any of them reliable. In al-Mabsut: The hadith is not authentic. Otherwise some would have used it as argument in the consultation with him when he said: “I am ashamed before Allah that I should leave him no hand to eat and clean himself with, and no foot to walk on.” And by this the rest of the Companions argued against him, and they defeated him, so consensus was established. And if it is granted that the hadith is authentic, it is interpreted as abrogated, because in the beginning there was severity in hudud punishments. Do you not see that the Prophet cut off the hands and feet of the ‘Urayniyin and gouged out their eyes, then that was abrogated. So reflect. (al-Qamar) Or the whole: i.e., the totality which is one legal unit. (al-Qamar) This hadith with this wording is strange. Al-Daraqutni produced in his Sunan, no. 292, 3/181, with the wording: “If the thief steals, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut off his foot; if he returns, cut off his hand; if he returns, cut off his foot” from Abu Hurayra. (al-Qamar) Explanation of the active participle like the command does not imply repetition, and all thefts are not known except at the end of life, so the one (single theft) is intended with certainty. And by one act only one hand is cut. Also “faqt’u” indicates cutting, and it also does not accept number. So the left hand is not established from the verse. It cannot be said that then the left foot should not be cut in the second instance either, because we say: The foot is not mentioned in the verse, so there is no harm if it is established by another text. As for the hand, since it is mentioned in the verse and the right hand is specifically intended from it, it is not permissible to establish the left hand by an isolated report (khabar al-wahid) which cannot add to the Book, because the specific locus (mahall) that is designated (i.e., the right hand) no longer exists. By consensus, unlike flogging: for whenever an unmarried person commits zina, he is flogged, because the body remains suitable for flogging always. Regarding ‘A’isha’s narration: “It is not known etc.” For if the intended meaning were all thefts, cutting the thief’s hand would have to wait until the end of life, which is invalid by consensus. (al-Qamar) “And by one act etc.”: Refutation of what might be imagined – cutting both hands for one theft. (al-Qamar) “Then it should not be cut etc.”: Because cutting does not accept number. (al-Qamar) “Then there is no harm if it is established etc.”: Thus said more than one. But it is flawed because the verse is addressing the hand, and the right is intended from it as will come. So just as the verse does not address the left foot, likewise it does not address the left hand, so it would be valid to establish cutting the left hand by another text just as it is valid to establish cutting the left foot by another text. So the distinction is arbitrary. The truth is to say: The establishment of cutting the left foot in the second instance is only by consensus, as Ibn al-Humam said. (al-Qamar) “Intended from it etc.”: i.e., by evidence of consensus, the sayings, and the actions, because the group except Ibn Majah produced the hadith of al-Makhzumiyyah, and in it: The Prophet ordered her right hand to be cut. And because al-Daraqutni narrated from Safwan ibn Umayyah, and in it: The Prophet cut the right hand of the thief from the wrist – thus said al-‘Alla’ al-Qari. And the reading of Ibn Mas’ud “aymanahuma” (their right hands) instead of “aydiyahuma” (their hands). (al-Qamar) “Because the locus has not remained etc.”: Evidence for his saying: “It is not permissible to establish etc.” (al-Qamar) “Unlike flogging etc.”: Indication to refute what may be imagined from His saying: “The fornicatress and the fornicator, flog each of them one hundred lashes” (an-Nur 24:2) – that the single fornication is intended by the proof mentioned in the verse on theft, so flogging should be done once. But it is not so, because if an unmarried person commits zina he is flogged, then if he commits zina after flogging, again and again. The essence of the refutation is that the locus of flogging is the body, and it remains suitable for flogging always. So whenever an unmarried person commits zina, he is flogged. This is of the type of repetition of the cause when the locus accepts repetition. Unlike theft, for the locus of cutting which is intended by consensus is the right hand. So when it is cut by the first theft, the locus no longer exists, so repetition cannot occur. Thus is derived from Bahr al-’Ulum, by lineage and knowledge – may Allah illuminate his resting place. He only said “unmarried” because the married one is stoned. Conditions for ihsan of stoning: freedom, sanity, puberty, Islam, and intercourse being in a valid marriage at the time of entry, and both being in the state of ihsan at the time of intercourse. So the ihsan of each is a condition for the other becoming muhsan – as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis and dispute from the Hanafi usul work Noor al-Anwar, commenting on the section on “al-Khass” (the specific). The author explains that the active participle (ism fa’il) does not imply repetition, similar to the command (amr). This principle is then applied to the verse on theft (al-Ma’idah 5:38) to argue that only one hand is cut per theft, contrary to the Shafi’i view that allows cutting the left hand in a third instance of theft. The passage begins by stating that the active participle indicates the masdar (source) by necessity, as in the example “anta taliq” (you are divorced), which only effects one divorce. It then addresses the Shafi’i position that the left hand and right foot are cut in subsequent thefts based on a hadith. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The hadith is not authentic, as argued by Ibn al-Humam and al-Tahawi, and even if authentic, it is abrogated due to earlier severity. (2) Even if the hadith were accepted, the term “al-sariq” (the thief) is an active participle, which linguistically points to a single action, so only one hand is cut per theft. The right hand is specifically indicated by consensus and other evidences (like the hadith of the Makhzumi woman and Ibn Mas’ud’s reading “aymanahuma”). The left hand cannot be added by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) because the verse already specifies the hand, and the locus (the right hand) is removed after the first cutting. A comparison with flogging for zina is made: flogging is repeatable because the body remains a suitable locus, whereas the hand is cut once. The passage concludes by stating that the left foot is cut in the second theft not from the verse but by consensus, and then the thief is imprisoned. The commentary thus demonstrates the Hanafi usul methodology of limiting textual implications and prioritizing consensus and the principle that ambiguous texts are interpreted narrowly.

Key Terms
اسم الفاعل (ism al-fa'il): The active participle, which indicates the agent of an action; in this text, it is argued to inherently imply a single occurrence of the action (the masdar) rather than repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view explained in this passage, what happens when a thief steals a third time after having his right hand and left foot cut?
A) His left hand is cut.
B) His right foot is cut.
C) He is imprisoned until he repents.
D) He is executed.

Key Takeaway
The active participle 'al-sariq' does not imply repetition, so only one hand (the right) is cut per theft; the left hand is never cut, and repeated theft leads to imprisonment not additional cutting.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Specific (Khas): Specifying the Thief's Hand
Dispute about whether the verse implies only the right hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a general Quranic term can be specified (takhsis) by consensus and sunnah, and derive the ruling that only the right hand is amputated for a first theft.

Core Idea
The Quranic 'hand' of the thief is specified as the right hand by consensus and prophetic sunnah.

In this passage, we see how a general Quranic verse is narrowed down using the tools of usul al-Fiqh. The verse commands cutting the hand of the thief, but which hand? The Hanafi school, relying on consensus and the practice of the Prophet, specifies it as the right hand. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and explores why the left hand cannot be cut for a first theft, and how this contrasts with flogging which can be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term in the verse
Locate the word 'aydiyahum' (أيديهما) in Al-Ma'idah 5:38 and classify it as general (amm) in usul al-fiqh.
The plural indicates generality, but it can be specified.
2
Recognize the specification (takhsis) by external evidence
Identify the specifiers: consensus of the ummah, the Prophet's cutting of the Makhzumiyyah's right hand, and the reading of Ibn Mas'ud (أيمانهما).
These are qat'i evidences that specify the general.
3
Understand why a solitary hadith cannot add the left hand
The verse's hand has been specified by consensus; adding the left hand by khabar wahid would be an increase upon the Book (ziyadah ala al-nass), which is impermissible.
The locus (mahal) is now specific to the right hand.
4
Contrast with flogging: why repetition is possible
Flogging can be repeated because the body remains a valid locus. For amputation, the locus (right hand) is removed after the first theft.
This distinction is based on the nature of the punishment.

مبحث الخاص بيان اسم الفاعل مثل الأمر لا يحتمل التكرار وكل السرقات لا يعلم إلا في آخر العمر ، فصار الواحد مرادًا بيقين، وبالفعل الواحد لا تقطع إلا يد واحدة، وأيضًا فاقطعوا دال على القطع وهو أيضًا لا يحتمل العدد، فلا تثبت اليد اليسرى من الآية لا يقال فينبغي أن لا تقطع الرجل اليسرى في الكرة الثانية أيضًا؛ لأنا نقول: إن الرجل غير متعرضة بها في الآية، فلا بأس أن يثبت بنص آخر، واليد لما كانت متعرضة بها في الآية، وتعين اليمنى مرادًا منها لا يجوز أن تثبت اليسرى بخبر الواحد الذي لا تجوز الزيادة به على الكتاب؛ لأنه لم يبق المحل المعين الذي تعين أي اليد اليمنى بالإجماع، بخلاف الجلد، فإنه كلما يزني غير المحصن يجلد؛ لأن البدن صالح للجلد دائما . عن عائشة في شأن لا يعلم إلخ فلو كان المراد كل السرقات لتوقف قطع السارق على آخر الحياة، وهو باطل بالإجماع. (القمر) وبالفعل إلخ: دفع لما يتوهم من قطع اليدين بسرقة واحدة. (القمر) فينبغي أن لا تقطع إلخ: لأن القطع لا يحتمل العدد (القمر) فلا بأس أن يثبت إلخ هكذا قال غير واحد ويخدشه أن الآية معترضة لليد، واليمنى مراد منها على ما سيجيء، فكما أن الآية غير متعرضة للرجل اليسرى كذلك غير متعرضة لليد اليسرى، فيصح إثبات قطع اليد اليسرى بنص آخر كما صح إثبات قطع الرجل اليسرى بنص ،آخر فالفرق تحكم، والحق أن يقال: إن إثبات قطع الرجل اليسرى في المرة الثانية إنما هو بالإجماع كما قال ابن الهمام له. (القمر) مرادًا منها إلخ: أي بدليل الإجماع والسنة القولية والفعلية لما أخرج الجماعة إلا ابن ماجة المخزومية، وفيه: فأمر النبي بقطع يمينها، ولما رواه الدار قطني من حديث صفوان ابن أمية، وفيه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قطع يمين السارق من الزند كذا قال العلي القاري، وقراءة ابن مسعود له أيمانهما مكان أيديهما. (القمر) لأنه لم يبق إلخ: دليل لقوله : لا يجوز أن تثبت إلخ. (القمر) بخلاف الجلد إلخ إشارة إلى دفع ما يتوهم من أن في قوله تعالى : الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحد مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَة (النور: ٢) يكون الزنا الواحد مرادا بالدليل المذكور في أية ،السرقة، فيجب الجلد مرة مع أنه ليس كذلك؛ إذ لو زنى غير المحصن يجلد، ثم لو زنى بعد الجلد ثم وثم وهكذا، وحاصل :الدفع أن محل الجلد هو البدن وهو باق صالح للجلد دائما فلما يزنى غير المحصن يجلد وهذا من قبيل تكرار السبب عند قبول المحل التكرار، بخلاف السرقة فإن محل القطع الذي أريد بالإجماع هي اليد ،اليمنى، فلما قطعت بالسرقة الأولى لم يبق المحل، فلا يتأدى التكرار، كذا أفيد من بحر العلوم أبي نسبًا وعلما نور الله مرقده، وإنما قال: غير المحصن؛ لأن المحصن يرجم، وشرائط إحصان الرجم: الحرية، والعقل، والبلوغ، والإسلام، والوطء، كون الوطء بنكاح صحيح حال الدخول، وكونهما بصفة الإحصان المذكورة وقت الوطء، فإحصان كل منهما شرط لصيرورة الآخر به محصنًا كذا في الدر المختار . (القمر)
Section on the Specific. Explanation of the active participle: like the command does not allow repetition, and all thefts are not known except at the end of life, so one becomes intended with certainty. And with one act, only one hand is cut. Also, 'cut off' indicates amputation, and it also does not allow number, so the left hand is not established from the verse. It cannot be said that the left foot should also not be cut in the second instance, because we say: the foot is not addressed in the verse, so there is no harm in establishing it by another text. And since the hand is addressed in the verse and the right is determined as intended, it is not permissible to establish the left by a solitary report that cannot increase upon the Book, because the specific locus that has been determined by consensus is no longer present. Unlike flogging, because whenever an unmarried person fornicates, he is flogged, because the body remains fit for flogging always. From Aisha regarding the matter: 'He does not know etc.' For if all thefts were intended, then cutting the thief would be postponed to the end of life, which is invalid by consensus. (Al-Qamar) 'And with the act etc.': a refutation of the misconception of cutting both hands for one theft. (Al-Qamar) 'Then the left foot should not be cut etc.': because cutting does not allow number. (Al-Qamar) 'So there is no harm in establishing etc.': thus said more than one, but it is flawed because the verse addresses the hand and the right is intended as will come, and just as the verse does not address the left foot, so too it does not address the left hand. So establishing the left hand by another text is valid, just as establishing the left foot by another text is valid. So the difference is arbitrary. The truth is that the establishment of cutting the left foot in the second instance is only by consensus as stated by Ibn al-Humam. (Al-Qamar) 'Intended from it etc.': that is by evidence of consensus and the oral and practical Sunnah, as reported by the group except Ibn Majah regarding the Makhzumiyyah: 'So the Prophet ordered cutting of her right hand', and as reported by al-Daraqutni from Safwan ibn Umayyah: 'The Prophet cut the right hand of the thief from the wrist.' Thus said al-Qari, and the reading of Ibn Mas'ud 'their right hands' instead of 'their hands'. (Al-Qamar) 'Because the locus is no longer present etc.': evidence for his statement that it is not permissible to establish etc. (Al-Qamar) 'Unlike flogging etc.': an indication of refuting the misconception that in the verse 'The fornicatress and the fornicator, flog each of them one hundred lashes' (al-Nur 2), one fornication would be intended by the same evidence mentioned in the verse on theft, so flogging would be required once, whereas it is not so. Because if an unmarried person fornicates, he is flogged; then if he fornicates after flogging, again and so on. The sum of the refutation is that the locus of flogging is the body, and it remains fit for flogging always. So whenever an unmarried person fornicates, he is flogged. This is of the category of repetition of the cause when the locus accepts repetition, unlike theft, for the locus of cutting which is intended by consensus is the right hand, so when it is cut by the first theft, the locus no longer remains, so repetition is not possible. Thus benefited from Bahr al-Ulum, Abu nasaban wa ilman, may Allah illuminate his grave. He said 'non-muhsan' only because the muhsan is stoned. Conditions for ihsan restricting to stoning: freedom, sanity, puberty, Islam, intercourse, that the intercourse be in a valid marriage at the time of entry, and that both be in the above-described state of ihsan at the time of intercourse. The ihsan of each is a condition for the other becoming muhsan thereby. As in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the principle of al-khas (the specific) as applied to the verse on theft (al-Ma'idah 38). The author begins by explaining that the verb 'cut off' does not imply repetition, and since a thief's total thefts are unknown until the end of life, the verse must refer to a single theft per amputation. Thus, only one hand is cut per theft. The question arises: does 'hand' include both right and left? The Hanafi position, based on consensus, the Prophet's practice, and Ibn Mas'ud's reading 'their right hands', is that only the right hand is intended. The objection that the left foot is also cut in a second offense is answered: the foot is not mentioned in the verse, so another text can establish it, but the hand is already specified by the verse, so a solitary hadith cannot override the Book's specification. The distinction from flogging is key: flogging can be repeated because the body remains. The passage also addresses conditions of ihsan for stoning. Throughout, the reasoning is anchored in usul al-fiqh concepts of 'amm, khass, and the use of consensus and sunnah to specify the general.

Key Terms
خاص (khas): A term that is specific in meaning, not general; here referring to the specific hand (right) intended by the verse.
يد (yad): Hand, but in the context of theft, it is specified as the right hand by consensus.
قطع (qat'): Amputation; the legal punishment for theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the hadith is weak.
B) Because the verse's hand has been specified to the right, and a solitary report cannot increase upon the Book.
C) Because the left hand is not mentioned in the Quran at all.
D) Because consensus prohibits cutting the left hand.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic amm can be specified by consensus and sunnah, and once specified, a solitary hadith cannot add another limb.

Defining Ada and Qada in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Defining ada and qada with necessary qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of ada and qada, explain the refinement replacing 'nafs' with 'ayn', and identify the exception for non-time-bound obligations.

Core Idea
Ada is performing the exact wajib in its time; qada is delivering its like later — but the like must come from your side, not Allah's.

In this passage from Noor al-Anwar, the author defines two key usul terms: ada (performance) and qada (make-up). The commentary then refines these definitions to avoid conceptual pitfalls, such as confusing qada with mere repetition of the same act. You will learn why the author replaced 'nafs al-wajib' with 'ayn al-wajib', why adding 'in its time' is unnecessary, and how an objection about qada being a 'like' from one's own side is resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base definitions
Read the opening lines: أداء is تسليم عين الواجب بالأمر, and قضاء is تسليم مثل الواجب بالأمر. Note that ada focuses on the identical wajib, qada on a like.
The definition of qada includes the phrase 'بعد الوقت' implicitly, as the passage explains.
2
Analyze the replacement of 'nafs' with 'ayn'
The author changed 'nafs al-wajib' to 'ayn al-wajib' to emphasize that ada is performing the act in its prescribed time, not the abstract obligation. The word 'ayn' metaphorically indicates presence in time.
This avoids the misconception that 'nafs' refers to the obligation itself.
3
Understand the objection about 'from his side'
A critic argues that qada should be qualified by 'من عنده' (from his side) to exclude cases like performing today's Zuhr as a make-up for yesterday's Zuhr. The commentator responds that the phrase 'مثل' already implies this, and it is well-known.
The example shows the need for precision: today's Zuhr cannot be qada because both prayers are obligations from Allah, not from the person's own side.
4
Note the exception of non-time-bound obligations
The passage observes that some wajibat, like zakat and kaffarat, are not time-bound yet the term 'ada' is used for them. This does not fit the strict definition, so it requires careful thought (تدبر).
This shows that definitions in usul may have exceptions in furu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حكم الواجب بالأمر بالتسليم لا بالواجب، ولهذا بدل المصنف له قوله : نفس الواجب بقوله: عين الواجب ليعلم أن نفس الواجب أو عينه كناية عن إتيانه في الوقت فلا حاجة إلى زيادة قوله : " في وقته" كما زاد البعض، وكذا إلى قوله: "إلى مستحقه"؛ لأن قوله : بالأمر يدل على أن الآمر هو المستحق. وقضاء وهو تسليم مثل الواجب ،به عطف على قوله : أداء بمعنى وجوب قضاء وهو تسليم مثل الواجب بالأمر لا عينه أي تسليم ذلك الواجب الذي وجب أوّلاً في غير ذلك الوقت، متعلق بالتسليم وكان ينبغي أن يقيده بقوله: من عنده ليخرج أداء ظهر اليوم قضاءً عن ظهر أمسه؛ لأنه ليس من عنده بل كلاهما لله تعالى، والقضاء إنما هو صرف النفل الذي كان حقا له إلى القضاء الذي كان عليه إنما لم يقيده به؛ لشهرة ،أمره، وكونه مدلولا عليه بالالتزام. ولهذا إلخ : أي لورود الاعتراض وإن كان قد أجيب عنه على كلام فخر الإسلام وكان منشأه لفظ النفس، بدل المصنف قوله نفس الواجب بقوله : عين الواجب؛ ليعلم أن نفس الواجب أو عينه كناية عن إتيانه في الوقت وليس المراد بنفس الوجوب ما هو مقابل لوجوب الأداء لا العين، وكذا النفس من ألفاظ التأكيد فيرفع احتمال المجاز فيحترز به عن مثل الواجب، وهو يكون في غير الوقت فعين الواجب يلزمه أن يكون في الوقت ولا يذهب عليك أن بعض المأمورات غير مؤقتة كالزكاة والكفارات ويطلق عليها لفظ الأداء يقال: أدي زكاة ماله وطعام كفارته، ولا يصدق عليه تعريف الأداء فتدبر. (القمر) فلا حاجة إلخ : تفريع على كون نفس الواجب أو عينه كناية عن إتيانه في الوقت. (القمر) وكذا إلى قوله إلخ : قال الحسامي: وهو تسليم عين الواجب بسببه إلى مستحقه أي إلى مستحق الواجب أو مستحق التسليم، فالمصنف لا حاجة له إلى قوله إلى مستحقه؛ لأن قوله إلخ، وأما الحسامي فمحتاج إليه. (القمر) ليخرج إلخ توضيحه أنه من صلى ظهر اليوم مثلاً أداء وعليه قضاء ظهر الأمس، فينبغي أن يقع أداء ظهر اليوم ظهر الأمس؛ لأنه يصدق عليه أنه تسليم مثل الواجب بالأمر مع أنه ليس كذلك، فكان ينبغي أن يقيد المصنف المثل في تعريف القضاء بقوله: من عنده كما قيد الحسامي؛ ليخرج أداء ظهر اليوم قضاء عن ظهر أمسه؛ لأن ظهر اليوم ليس من عند المأمور بل كلاهما أي ظهر اليوم وظهر الأمس الله تعالى فرضان على المأمور، والقضاء إنما هو صرف النفل الذي هو حق للمأمور إلى القضاء الذي كان ضروريًا على المأمور وهو لم يوجد ههنا، وإنما لم يقيد المصنف المثل بقوله : من عنده لشهرته، ولدلالة لفظ المثل عليه بالالتزام فإن المراد بالمثل ما ثبت وهو إنما يكون من عنده. (القمر) قضاء عن الفائت عوضا عن
Explanation of the ruling of the obligatory by command through delivery, not by the obligatory itself. For this reason, the author replaced his phrase 'the very wajib' with 'the identical wajib' to indicate that 'the very wajib' or 'the identical wajib' is a metaphor for performing it in its time, so there is no need to add 'in its time' as some did, nor to add 'to its rightful claimant' because his phrase 'by command' indicates that the commander is the rightful claimant. Qada: it is delivering the like of the wajib, connected to his saying 'ada' meaning obligation of qada, i.e., delivering the like of the wajib by command, not the identical one, i.e., delivering that wajib which was originally obligatory in another time. It was necessary to qualify it with 'from his side' to exclude performing today's zuhr as a make-up for yesterday's zuhr; because it is not from his side, both belong to Allah, and qada is merely converting the supererogatory which was his right into the make-up that was upon him. He did not qualify it due to its fame and being implied. 'For this reason etc.': i.e., to answer the objection, though it was answered in the words of Fakhr al-Islam, its origin was the word 'nafs'. The author replaced 'nafs al-wajib' with 'ayn al-wajib' to indicate that 'nafs al-wajib' or 'ayn al-wajib' is metaphorical for performing in time, not that 'nafs' is opposite to 'obligation of ada'. 'Nafs' is an emphasis, removing possibility of metaphor, guarding against 'mithl al-wajib' which occurs outside the time. 'Ayn al-wajib' necessitates being in time. Note that some commanded acts are not time-bound like zakat and expiations, and the word 'ada' is used for them, e.g., 'he performed the zakat of his wealth', yet the definition of ada does not apply to them, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'So there is no need etc.': a branch on 'nafs al-wajib' or 'ayn al-wajib' being metaphorical for performing in time. (al-Qamar) 'And similarly to his saying etc.': al-Husami said: it is delivering the identical wajib by its cause to its rightful claimant, i.e., to the one entitled to the wajib or the delivery. So the author has no need for 'to its rightful claimant' because his saying etc., but al-Husami is in need of it. (al-Qamar) 'To exclude etc.': explanation: if someone performs today's zuhr as ada and owes qada of yesterday's zuhr, performing today's zuhr should count as qada for yesterday's zuhr because it fits the definition of delivering the like of the wajib by command, but it is not so. So the author should have qualified 'mithl' in the definition of qada with 'from his side' as al-Husami did, to exclude performing today's zuhr as qada for yesterday's zuhr; because today's zuhr is not from the commanded person's side, both are due to Allah. Qada is only converting the supererogatory that is the right of the commanded person to the qada that was necessary upon him, which does not occur here. The author did not qualify 'mithl' with 'from his side' due to its fame and because the word 'mithl' implies it, for 'mithl' means what is established, and it is only from his side. (al-Qamar) Qada for the missed [prayer] as a substitute.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a definition and refinement of the Hanafi usul terms ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up). The author of Noorul Anwar initially defines ada' as delivering the wajib by command, and qada' as delivering the like of the wajib by command. The commentator then discusses necessary clarifications: first, the replacement of 'nafs al-wajib' with 'ayn al-wajib' to show that the focus is on performing the identical act in its prescribed time, not the abstract obligation. Second, there is no need to add 'in its time' because the phrase 'by command' already indicates the commander's right to set the time. Third, there is no need to add 'to its rightful claimant' because the command implies the commander is the recipient. Fourth, the critic argues that 'like' in the definition of qada' should be qualified with 'from his side' to avoid counting the performance of today's zuhr as a make-up for yesterday's zuhr, since both are obligatory on the person and not from his own side (i.e., not his own property). The commentator refutes this by noting that 'like' is well-known to mean something that comes from the person's own side, implied by the term. The passage ends with a marginal note 'Qada for the missed as a substitute', which may be a heading.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-ada'): تسليم عين الواجب بالأمر
القضاء (al-qada'): تسليم مثل الواجب بالأمر
عين الواجب (ayn al-wajib): the identical wajib (metaphor for performing in its time)
مثل الواجب (mithl al-wajib): like of the wajib

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author replace 'nafs al-wajib' with 'ayn al-wajib'?
A) To indicate that the act must be performed in its time
B) To emphasize the obligation itself
C) To include supererogatory acts
D) To avoid metaphor

Key Takeaway
Ada and qada are distinguished by time and identity: ada requires the exact wajib in time; qada requires a like, which implies it comes from the person's own side.

Metaphorical Interchange of Ada' and Qada'
Usul definition of metaphorical interchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi usul principle that ada' and qada' can be used metaphorically for each other, state the condition of a contextual indicator (qarina), and apply this to Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Ada' and qada' are linked by a shared meaning of fulfilling an obligation, allowing legal metaphor.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the terms 'ada'' (performance in time) and 'qada''' (making up after time) are defined distinctly. However, the scholars recognized that they can be used interchangeably in a metaphorical sense due to a common core of 'delivering what is due.' This lesson unpacks that principle, its conditions, and its evidence from the Qur'an and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definitions
Recall the Hanafi definitions: ada' is performing the exact obligation within its time; qada' is delivering its like after the time. Note the shared element of 'taslim' (delivery).
The distinction is critical for intention.
2
Establish the metaphorical link
The text states that one can be used in place of the other metaphorically (majāz sharʿī) because both involve delivering something to its rightful owner and fulfilling an obligation.
This is not literal interchange; it requires a contextual indicator (qarīna).
3
Apply to Quranic examples
Examine the verses: Q.2:200 (فَإِذَا قَضَيْتُمْ مَنَاسِكَكُمْ) uses qada' in the sense of ada'; Q.62:10 (فَإِذَا قُضِيَتِ الصَّلَاةُ) uses qada' to mean performing the prayer.
The context indicates performance, not making up.
4
Understand the condition for validity
Metaphorical usage is valid only when literal usage is impossible or requires a qarina. For example, one can intend 'qada'' while performing ada' if a contextual indicator exists (e.g., saying 'I intend to perform qada of today's prayer' is permissible because the time is still present).
The intention must correspond to the actual situation; mere words without reality are insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(القمر) وفيه وجوه أخر: أي لدفع ما يرد على تعريف الأداء منها: أن إطلاق الأداء على أداء النفل توسع على ما عليه عامة الفقهاء والتعريف للأداء الحقيقي فلا ضير، ومنها أن أداء النفل وإن كان أداء لكن الكلام ليس في مطلق الأداء بل فيما هو موجب للأمر عندنا فالمعرف خاص. (القمر) مجازا أي مجازًا شرعيًا؛ لتباين المعنيين مع اشتراكهما في تسليم الشيء إلى من يستحقه وفي إسقاط الواجب كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا قَضَيْتُمْ مناسككُمْ (البقرة: ٢٠٠) أي أديتم وقولك: أديت الدين، قيدنا بالشرعي؛ لأنه بحسب اللغة القضاء حقيقة في تسليم العين والمثل؛ لأن معناه الإسقاط والإتمام والإحكام، والأداء محاز في تسليم المثل؛ لأنه ينبئ عن شدة الرعاية والاستقصاء في الخروج عما لزمه، وذلك بتسليم العين دون المثل كذا في "التلويح". [فتح الغفار ٥٠] حتى يجوز إلخ لما كان يرد عليه أن هذا التفريع لا يصح فإن النية فعل القلب لا استعمال لفظ فيها، ولا يلزم من صحة استعمال كل من الأداء والقضاء مكان الآخر قيام نية كل منهما مقام نية الآخر اختار أعظم العلماء أن هذا تأييد لصحة استعمال أحدهما مكان الآخر لا تفريع عليها، وجواز الأداء بنية القضاء كجواز أداء صلاة من ظن خروج الوقت ونوى القضاء وفي الواقع لم يخرج وقتها، وجواز القضاء بنية الأداء كجواز قضاء من ظن بقاء وقت الصلاة ونوى الأداء وفي الواقع لم يبق وقتها واختار صاحب كشف البزدوي" أن هذا تفريع، والمراد بجواز الأداء بنية القضاء أن يذكر لفظ القضاء في النية لفظا ويراد به الأداء، وبجواز القضاء بنية الأداء أن يذكر لفظ الأداء في النية لفظًا ويراد به القضاء، وتبعه الشارح له حيث قال في الموضعين فيما سيأتي بأن يقول إلخ، والعجب من بحر العلوم أنه اكتفى بذكر الإيراد في "التنوير".(القمر)
بيان تقسيم الوجوب كل من الأداء والقضاء مكان الآخر بطريق المجاز حتى يجوز الأداء بنية القضاء بأن يقول: فلابد من قرينة في وقت الظهور نويتُ أن أقضي ظهر اليوم، ويجوز القضاء بنية الأداء بأن يقول: نويت أن أؤدي ظهر الأمس، واستعمال القضاء في الأداء كثير كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا قُضِيَتِ الصَّلاةُ فَانْتَشِرُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ أي إذا أديت صلاة الجمعة لا تقضى، ولذا ذهب فخر الإسلام إلى أن القضاء (الجمعة: ١٠) عام يستعمل في الأداء والقضاء جميعًا؛ لأنه عبارة عن فراغ الذمة وهو يحصل بهما، فكان في معنى الحقيقة، بخلاف الأداء ينبئ عن شدة الرعاية وهو ليس إلا في الأداء كما قال الشاعر : الذئب يأدو للغزال يأكله أي يختله ويغلب عليه، وأما إذا صام شعبان بظن أنه من رمضان فلا يجوز؛ لأنه أداء قبل السبب، وإن صام شوال بظن أنه من رمضان يجوز وهو شهود رمضان أن أقضي أي أن أؤدي بقرينة وجود الوقت . (القمر) أن أودي أي أقضي؛ لأن أداء ظهر الأمس بعد مضيه محال. (القمر) واستعمال القضاء إلخ لما بين أولاً أن أحدهما يستعمل في مقام الآخر، فمن ههنا يبين أن استعمال كل مقام الآخر ليس على السواء بل فيه التفاوت ثابت فإن استعمال القضاء في الأداء كثير وعكسه قليل (السنبلي) ولذا أي لكون استعمال القضاء في الأداء كثيرًا. (القمر) أي يختله رأيت في النسخة المكتوبة بيد الشارح أي يختاله. (القمر) وأما إذا صام إلخ : دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن الأداء لما كان فيه شدة الرعاية، فينبغي أن يجوز إذا صام شعبان يظن أنه من رمضان؛ لأنه تعجل في تعيين المأمور به مع أنه لا يجوز ، وتقرير الدفع أن الصائم لو تكلم ههنا بلفظ الأداء أو القضاء لا يجوز أصلاً لا بالمعنى الحقيقى ولا بالمجازي؛ لأنه لم يوجد محلها كما إذا قال لزوجته الكبيرة: "هذه بنتي" فعلى هذا هو جواب أيضًا للسؤال الذي قرر بأن استعمال كل مقام الآخر مجاز ، وشرطه تعذر الحقيقة، ففي صورة صوم رجل من شعبان بظن أنه من رمضان كان الأداء متعذرًا فينبغي أن يصار إلى المجاز وهو القضاء. (السنبلي)
As for the voluntary (nafl), it is only made up (qada') if it becomes binding by commencing, and then it is no longer voluntary but becomes obligatory. However, it is performed (ada') while it is not obligatory. So it should be intended by 'the exact obligatory (thing) established' to include the voluntary; thus it was said, and there are other aspects.
And one is used in place of the other metaphorically, so that it is permissible to perform (ada') with the intention of making up (qada') and vice versa. That is, it uses qada' which is ada'... and so on.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion in Hanafi usul al-fiqh about the terms 'ada'' (performance) and 'qada''' (making up). It begins by addressing a potential objection regarding voluntary acts: when one starts a voluntary act, it becomes binding, so its completion is technically qada' but performed as ada'. The author then clarifies that ada' and qada' can be used metaphorically for each other due to a shared meaning of fulfilling an obligation. The text cites Quranic verses (2:200 and 62:10) as examples where qada' is used in the sense of ada'. It also discusses the conditions for this metaphorical usage, such as the need for a contextual indicator (qarina). The commentary mentions different scholarly opinions from Fakhral-Islam and others. The passage concludes with an example: if someone fasts in Sha'ban thinking it is Ramadan, it is not valid because it is performance before the cause; but if they fast in Shawwal thinking it is Ramadan, it is valid as qada'. This illustrates the rules for metaphorical interchange.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-adā'): Performance of an act of worship in its prescribed time as initially obligated
القضاء (al-qadā'): Making up an obligatory act after its time has passed
المجاز (al-majāz): Metaphorical usage; here used in the sense of shar'i (legal) metaphor because the two terms share a common meaning of delivering something
القرينة (al-qarīna): Contextual indicator that clarifies the intended meaning when metaphorical usage is employed

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is necessary for the metaphorical use of 'ada' ' in the sense of 'qada' ' according to the Hanafi scholars in this passage?
A) The act must be voluntary (nafl).
B) The intention must be expressed verbally.
C) There must be a contextual indicator (qarina).
D) The time for the prayer must have definitely passed.

Key Takeaway
Ada' and qada' can be used metaphorically for each other in Hanafi usul, but only when a contextual indicator is present, with qada' being more common in the sense of ada' than the reverse.

Types of Qada: Pure Qada and the Rational Similar Dispute
Definition and classification of qada with a dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two subtypes of pure qada (rational similar and non-rational similar) and explain why the Hanafi school holds that qada with a rational similar does not require a new cause.

Core Idea
Pure qada has two subtypes; only non-rational similar needs a new cause — the dispute is on rational similar.

In this passage from Noorul Anwar, the author turns from performance (ada) to making up (qada). He presents a three-part classification: pure qada subdivided into rational and non-rational similar, and qada that resembles performance. The key legal disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is centers on whether a rational similar (e.g., fasting for fasting) requires a new cause. We will work through the classification and the underlying usul principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main types of qada
The passage initially lists three types: with rational similar, with non-rational similar, and in the meaning of ada. Then it refines this into 'pure qada' (two subtypes) and 'qada fi ma'na al-ada'. Mark these clearly.
Pure qada has no element of performance at all.
2
Distinguish rational similar from non-rational similar
Rational similar: reason perceives similarity without revelation (e.g., fasting replaces fasting). Non-rational similar: similarity is known only from sharia (e.g., fidyah replaces fasting). Understand the epistemological basis.
Reason does not contradict the non-rational; it just can't perceive the similarity.
3
Locate the area of agreement and disagreement
All schools agree: pure qada (both subtypes) requires a new cause? No! The text says: 'This qada necessarily requires a new cause by agreement' referring to non-rational similar. The disagreement is only on rational similar.
Check the Arabic carefully: 'وهذا القضاء لابد فيه من سبب جديد بالاتفاق' refers to non-rational similar.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof for rational similar
The Hanafi argument: the obligation remains on the liability until performed or waived; performing the same type (rational similar) is simply the delayed fulfillment of the same obligation, so no new cause is needed. Find this in the text.
The example of fasting for fasting illustrates the continuity of obligation.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i counterposition and the thamarah al-khilaf
Shafi'is hold that qada is a new obligation, hence requires a new command or intention. The practical consequence: a Hanafi can make up a missed fast with a general intent to make up qada, while a Shafi'i needs a specific separate intention.
This difference affects daily practice in observing make-up fasts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ عن بيان أنواع الأداء شرع في تقسيم القضاء، فقال: والقضاء أنواع أيضًا بمثل معقول، وبمثل غير معقول، وما هو في معنى الأداء، وفي هذا التقسيم أيضًا مسامحة، وكأنه قيل: والقضاء أنواع : قضاء محض وهو إما بمثل معقول أو بمثل غير معقول، وقضاء في معنى الأداء، ويُعنى بالقضاء المحض ما لا يكون فيه معنى الأداء أصلاً لا حقيقةً ولا حكمًا. والمراد بالمثل المعقول: أن تدرك مماثلته بالعقل مع قطع النظر عن الشرع، وبغير المعقول: أن لا تدرك المماثلة إلا شرعًا، ويكون العقل قاصرًا عن درك كيفيته لا أن العقل يناقضه، وهذا القضاء لابد فيه من سبب جديد بالاتفاق، وإنما الخلاف في القضاء بمثل معقول. كالصوم للصوم، هذا نظير للقضاء بمثل معقول أي كقضاء الصوم للصوم، فإنه أمر معقول؛ لأن الواجب لا يسقط عن الذمة إلا بالأداء أو بإسقاط صاحب الحق، وما لم يوجد أحدهما يبقى في ذمته. والفدية له، هذا نظير للقضاء بمثل غير معقول، فإن الفدية بمقابلة الصوم لا يدركه عقل؛ إذ لا مماثلة بينهما صورة، وهو ظاهر ولا معنى؛ لأن الصوم تجويع النفس، والفدية إشباع.
When he finished explaining the types of performance (ada), he began dividing qada (making up), and said: Qada also has types: with a rational similar, with a non-rational similar, and what is in the meaning of performance. In this division there is also some tolerance, as if it were said: Qada is of types: pure qada, which is either with a rational similar or with a non-rational similar, and qada in the meaning of performance. By pure qada is meant that in which there is no meaning of performance at all, neither in reality nor in ruling. And by rational similar is meant that its similarity is perceived by reason independently of revelation; by non-rational similar is meant that similarity is perceived only by revelation, and reason is incapable of perceiving its modality—not that reason contradicts it. This qada necessarily requires a new cause by agreement, but the disagreement is concerning qada with a rational similar. For example, fasting for fasting: this is an example of qada with a rational similar, i.e., making up fasting with fasting, for it is rational, because an obligation is not discharged from the liability except by performance or by the waiver of the right-holder, and unless one of these occurs it remains in his liability. And fidyah for it: this is an example of qada with a non-rational similar, for the fidyah in exchange for fasting is not perceived by reason, since there is no similarity between them in form—this is apparent—and not in meaning, because fasting is starving the soul, while fidyah is feeding.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of qada (making up) as a usul concept. The author first states that after discussing ada (performance), he now turns to qada. He divides qada into three types: pure qada (qada mahd) which contains no element of performance, and qada that is in the meaning of performance. Pure qada is further subdivided into two: with a rational similar (mithl ma'qul) and with a non-rational similar (mithl ghayr ma'qul). The rational similar is one where reason can perceive the similarity without relying on revelation—like making up a missed fast by fasting; it is rationally obvious that the same act suffices. The non-rational similar is one where similarity is established only by revelation, such as fidyah (feeding a poor person) as a substitute for fasting; reason sees no inherent similarity between fasting and feeding. The author emphasizes that for pure qada—both types—a new cause is required by all schools; the disagreement is only about qada with a rational similar. The commentary (likely from the sharh) clarifies that the Hanafi position is supported by the principle that an obligation remains in the liability until performed or waived, so no new cause is needed—unlike the Shafi'i view which requires a new cause even with a rational similar. The example of fasting versus fidyah illustrates the rational versus non-rational distinction. The author also notes that the classification is not without some tolerance (musamaha), meaning it is not absolutely precise but serves pedagogical purposes.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qaḍāʾ): Making up an obligatory act that was missed, performed after its time.
المثل المعقول (al-mithl al-maʿqūl): A type of qada where the similarity between the missed act and its replacement is rationally understood, e.g., fasting for fasting.
المثل غير المعقول (al-mithl ghayr al-maʿqūl): A type of qada where similarity is established only by revelation (sharia), e.g., fidyah for fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in the text, why does qada with a rational similar NOT require a new cause?
A) Because the original obligation is waived by the passage of time.
B) Because the obligation remains on the liability until performed or forgiven.
C) Because the similar act is different from the original.
D) Because all scholars agree on this point.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of qada distinguishes rational similar (no new cause needed) from non-rational similar (new cause agreed), with the dispute centered on the former due to the nature of obligation.

Prioritizing Compensation by Mithl over Qima in Ghasb
Commentary on qada with mithl and qima for maghsub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that compensation for a usurped fungible (mithli) good must be made with its identical equivalent (mithl) if available, and identify when qima is permissible.

Core Idea
For fungible goods, full compensation requires the exact same thing; value is only accepted when the mithl is unavailable.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary clarifies the hierarchy in compensating for a usurped item. It distinguishes between fungible goods (mithli) and non-fungibles (qimi), and explains why the identical item takes precedence over its monetary value. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying Hanafi rulings in property disputes and commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is ghasb (usurpation) of a mithli good. The ruling: compensation must be by mithl (identical equivalent) if it is available. If not, compensation is by qima (value).
2
Define mithli and qimi
A mithli is a good for which an identical equivalent exists in the market without significant difference, e.g., wheat, barley, eggs. A qimi is a good with no standard equivalent, e.g., animals, real estate, clothes.
Hanafi definition emphasizes market availability; some scholars add weight/measure criteria.
3
Apply the hierarchy: mithl over qima
The text states that the mithl is 'prior' (sabiq) because it provides complete compensation in both form and meaning. The qima only provides compensation in meaning. Therefore, as long as the mithl exists, the owner cannot be compelled to accept the value.
This is a firm rule: the usurper must deliver the mithl; offering value is insufficient.
4
Identify when qima becomes acceptable
The passage indicates that qima is used either when the item has no mithl (qimi) or when the mithl has disappeared from the market (insarama). In such cases, compensation by value is the substitute.
Even if the mithl exists in private homes but not in the market, it is considered unavailable.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may have a broader definition of mithli or allow more flexibility in accepting value. Hanafis strictly require mithl for fungibles, affecting how courts order restitution.
This distinction is crucial for fatwa: a Hanafi mufti will insist on the identical item, not its cash equivalent, if available.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بيان أنواع القضاء وهو عند الله اللحم المذكى المراق منه الدم ليكون أول تناول الناس من طعام الضيافة المكرمة، فما دام كانت الأيام موجودةً، قلنا: إن التضحية أصل برأسها وعملنا بالمنصوص، وإذا فاتت الأيام صرنا إلى الأصل، وقلنا: إن التصدق بعين الشاة أو بالقيمة هو الأصل، فحكمنا به، ثم إذا جاء العام الثاني لم ننتقل من هذا الحكم و لم نقل بقضائها على ما كان في العام الأول. ثم لما فرغ المصنف من بيان أنواع القضاء في حقوق الله تعالى شرع في بيان أنواعه في حقوق العباد فقال ومنها ضمان المغصوب بالمثل وهو السابق، أو بالقيمة أي من أنواع القضاء ضمان الشيء المغصوب بالمثل فيما إذا غصب مثليًا واستهلكه ووجد المثل وهو عند الله اللحم إلخ توضيحه أن مال الصدقة من الأوساخ لإزالته الذنوب، وإليه يشير قوله تعالى: {خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةً تُطَهِّرُهُمْ} (التوبة: ١٠٣) ولهذا حرم الصدقة على النبي ، وعلى من لحق به نسبا؛ لكرامتهم، وعلى الغني؛ لعدم كونه محتاجًا وليس اللائق للكريم الغني أن يضيف عباده بالمال الخبيث فنقلنا عنه إلى التضحية لينتقل الخبث إلى الدماء، واللحوم بقيت طيبة، وبها تحققت الضيافة من الله تعالى لعباده. (القمر) ليكون أول إلخ ولذا يستحب يوم النحر تأخير الأكل إلى الصلاة، وما قيل تبعًا لشارح الحسامي: من أن الأكل قبل الصلاة مكروه، ففيه أنه لا يلزم الكراهة من ترك المستحب كذا قال الطحطاوي، وقال شارح "المنية": والأصح أنه لا يكره الأكل قبل الصلاة ههنا (القمر) بالمنصوص أي بما ورد به النص وهو قوله عليك "ضحوا فإنها سنة أبيكم إبراهيم". بيان أنواع القضاء
فيما بين الناس أو بالقيمة فيما لم يكن له مثل أو كان له مثل ولكن انصرم عن أيدي الناس، فهذا نظير القضاء بمثل معقول ؛ لأن المثل والقيمة كلاهما مثل معقول، أما الأول فظاهر؛ إذ هو مثل صورةً ،ومعنى، وأما الثاني فهو أيضا مثل معنى و إن لم يكن صورة، ولكن الأول كامل والثاني قاصر ولهذا قال: وهو السابق أي المثل الصوري سابق على المثل المعنوي، فما دام وُجد المثل الصوري لم ينتقل إلى المثل المعنوي، ففيه تنبيه على أن القضاء بمثل معقول نوعان كامل وقاصر، لا يقال مثل هذا متحقق في حقوق الله تعالى أيضًا، فإن قضاء الصلاة بالجماعة كامل، وقضاءها منفردًا قاصر، فلم لم يتعرض له؛ لأنا نقول : عندهم قضاء الصلاة منفردًا كامل وبالجماعة أكمل
أو بالقيمة إلخ معطوف على قوله بالمثل (القمر) ولكن انصرم أي انقطع عن أيدي الناس بأن لا يوجد في السوق الذي يباع فيه وإن كان يوجد في البيوت كذا في الدر المختار". (القمر) ومعنى المثل معنى عبارة عن قيمة الشيء أي عن قدر ماليته بالدراهم والدنانير. (القمر) ولكن إلخ استدراك عن قوله: كلاهما مثل معقول. (القمر) سابق على المثل :إلخ لأن الضمان واجب بطريق الجبر، والجبر التام أن يتداركه بأداء مال من عنده هو مثل لما فوت عليه صورة ومعنى كالحنطة للحنطة حتى يقوم مقام المغصوب من كل وجه فكان مقدمًا على المثل معنى وثمرة كونه سابقا أنه لو أدى القيمة في غصب المثلى مع القدرة على المثل الكامل بأن يوجد في الأسواق لا يجبر المالك على القبول. (السنبلي) لم ينتقل إلخ إذ حق المالك في الصورة والمعنى، والمقصود جبر حقه فيراعى فيهما ما أمكن، فلو أدى القيمة فيما إذا غصب مثليًا مع القدرة على المثل الصوري بأن يوجد في الأسواق لا يجبر المالك على القبول.(القمر) ففيه تنبيه إلخ هذا دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن من كلام الماتن السابق أي قوله والقضاء أنواع أيضًا إلخ يفهم أن طريق تقسيمه إلى الأقسام الثلاثة مثل طريق تقسيم الأداء إليها أي لا يزيد أقسامه على الثلاثة كما لا يزيد أقسام الأداء عليها، فعلى هذا كان ينبغي للمصنف أن يكتفي بأمثال ثلاثة للأقسام الثلاثة، فلم زاد مثالاً على الثلاثة، فأجاب بأنه زاده للتنبيه على أن القضاء إلخ كان أقسام القضاء الأولية مثل عدد أقسام الأداء لا أقسامه مطلقًا. (السنبلي) مثل هذا أي تقسيم القضاء بمثل معقول إلى كامل وقاصر. (القمر) منفردًا كامل لأن الكمال هو العمل على ما شرح عليه وجبرائيل عليه لم يعلم القضاء بالجماعة حتى يكون على الانفراد قاصرًا بل علم الأداء بالجماعة، فالأداء بالجماعة كامل، ومنفردًا قاصر وليس كذلك القضاء، =
Section on the Specific. Explanation of the types of qada (compensation/fulfillment). And it is with Allah the meat of the sacrificed animal from which blood is let flow to be the first thing people partake of from the food of the honored feast. So as long as the days (of sacrifice) exist, we said: 'Indeed, sacrifice is a separate original obligation, and we act according to the explicit text.' And when the days pass, we revert to the original, and we said: 'Indeed, giving charity in the form of the same sheep or its value is the original, so we ruled accordingly.' Then when the second year comes, we do not move from this ruling, and we do not say to make it up (qada) as it was in the first year. Then when the author finished explaining the types of qada in the rights of Allah Most High, he began explaining its types in the rights of servants and said: 'And among them is the guarantee of the usurped item by its mithl (identical equivalent), which is the prior, or by its value.' That is, among the types of qada is the guarantee of the stolen item by its mithl in case one usurped a fungible (mithli) item and consumed it and finds the mithl. 'And it is with Allah the meat...' etc. Its clarification: that the wealth of charity is from filth because it removes sins, as Allah's verse indicates: 'Take from their wealth a charity to purify them' (9:103). Hence charity was forbidden to the Prophet and to those related to him by lineage due to their honor, and to the wealthy because they are not needy. And it is not fitting for the generous wealthy person to host His servants with filthy wealth, so we transferred from it to sacrifice so that the filth transfers to the blood, and the meat remains pure, and by it the hosting from Allah to His servants is realized. (al-Qamar) 'to be the first' etc. Therefore, on the Day of Sacrifice, it is recommended to delay eating until after the prayer. What was said following the commentator of al-Husami: that eating before prayer is disliked (makruh) — it is said that dislike does not follow from abandoning the recommended. Thus said al-Tahtawi. And the commentator of al-Munyah said: 'The correct view is that eating before prayer is not disliked here.' (al-Qamar) 'by the explicit text': i.e., by what is stated in the text, which is his saying: 'Sacrifice, for it is the sunnah of your father Ibrahim.' (al-Qamar) 'Then when it comes' etc.: A rebuttal of an anticipated objection: that if the obligation of either the same sheep or its value were due to caution as in the text, then sacrifice should be obligatory when the days of sacrifice come in the second year before giving charity due to caution. The rebuttal: when the second year comes, we do not move from this ruling (i.e., the obligation to give charity with the same sheep or its value) to sacrifice, and we do not say to make up the sacrifice in this second year as was the case in the first year. Do you not see that if an ijtihad has passed with its ruling, a subsequent ijtihad does not change it? (al-Qamar) The first: because the obligation of giving charity is due to the probability of originality, not by way of deputyship. (al-Muhashshi) Giving charity. Types of qada: i.e., pure qada with a rational equivalent, and qada in the sense of performance. (al-Qamar) 'mithli' (fungible): Know that a mithli is that for which an equivalent exists in the markets without significant difference, and what is not like that is a qimi (non-fungible), such as animals, firewood, real estate, clothes, watermelon, wages, wheat, barley and their likes are mithli. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. And the greatest scholars (i.e., our master Abd al-Salam al-A'zami) said: 'What is meant by mithli is what is measured by weight, volume, or countable with close numbers like eggs and almonds.' (al-Qamar) Explanation of types of qada among people: or by value when there is no mithl, or there is a mithl but it has disappeared from the hands of people. So this is analogous to qada with a rational equivalent, because both the mithl and the value are a rational equivalent. As for the first, it is apparent, for it is an equivalent in form and meaning. As for the second, it is also an equivalent in meaning even if not in form, but the first is complete and the second deficient. For this reason he said: 'and it is the prior', i.e., the mithl in form is prior to the mithl in meaning. Thus as long as the mithl in form exists, one does not move to the mithl in meaning. In this is an indication that qada with a rational equivalent is of two types: complete and deficient. It cannot be said that such a thing is also realized in the rights of Allah Most High, for the qada of prayer in congregation is complete, and its qada alone is deficient. So why did he not address it? We answer: According to them, the qada of prayer alone is complete, and in congregation is more complete. 'Or by value' etc. is conjoined to his statement 'by the mithl'. (al-Qamar) 'but has disappeared (insarama)': i.e., it has ceased from the hands of people such that it is not found in the market where it is sold, even if it exists in houses. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (al-Qamar) And 'mithl in meaning' is an expression for the value of the thing, i.e., the amount of its monetary worth in dirhams and dinars. (al-Qamar) 'But' etc. is an istidrak (corrective continuation) from his statement: 'Both are a rational equivalent.' (al-Qamar) 'Prior to the mithl' etc.: Because guarantee is obligatory by way of compensation, and complete compensation is to make up by paying from oneself wealth that is like what was lost in form and meaning, like wheat for wheat, so that it stands in place of the usurped item in every respect. Thus it is given precedence over the mithl in meaning. The consequence of it being prior is that if one pays the value in the case of usurping a mithli while being able to pay the complete mithl (i.e., it exists in the markets), the owner is not compelled to accept. (al-Sunbuli) 'does not move' etc.: Since the right of the owner is in form and meaning, and the aim is to compensate his right, so both are taken into account as much as possible. So if one pays the value in the case of usurping a mithli while able to pay the mithl in form (i.e., it exists in the markets), the owner is not compelled to accept. (al-Qamar) 'In this is an indication' etc.: This is a rebuttal of an anticipated objection: from the author's earlier statement 'And qada is also of types ...' it is understood that his method of dividing it into three types is like the method of dividing performance into them, i.e., its types do not exceed three just as the types of performance do not exceed them. Accordingly, the author should have sufficed with three examples for the three types. So why did he add an example beyond three? He answered: He added it for the indication that the primary types of qada are like the number of types of performance, not its types absolutely. (al-Sunbuli) 'Such as this': i.e., dividing qada with a rational equivalent into complete and deficient. (al-Qamar) 'Alone is complete': Because completeness is acting according to what has been explained, and Jibril عليه السلام did not know qada in congregation such that being alone would be deficient; rather, he knew performance in congregation. So performance in congregation is complete, and alone is deficient. It is not so for qada. =
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on a matn discussing the types of qada (compensation or fulfillment), specifically focusing on the guarantee of a usurped item (daman al-maghsub) in the rights of servants. The author explains that qada can be with the exact same thing (mithl) or its value (qima). The commentary begins by drawing an analogy with the rights of Allah, using the example of sacrifice (udhiyah) and charity (sadaqah). It clarifies that when the days of sacrifice are present, the obligation is to sacrifice; when they pass, one must give the same animal or its value in charity. This reasoning is applied to ghasb: if a person usurps a mithli (fungible) good and it is still available, the compensation must be with that same mithl. If the mithl is not available (e.g., it has disappeared from the market), then compensation is with its value. The commentary also distinguishes between mithli and qimi goods, defining mithli as goods for which identical equivalents exist in the market without significant difference (e.g., wheat, barley, eggs, almonds). Qimi goods (e.g., animals, real estate) are compensated by value. The author then discusses the priority of mithl over qima, explaining that the mithl represents complete compensation in both form and meaning, while the value is only in meaning. Therefore, as long as the mithl exists, the owner cannot be compelled to accept the value. A similar hierarchical distinction is made for qada in acts of worship: for example, qada of prayer in congregation is considered more complete than alone, but the text notes that according to the school, qada alone is still considered complete, only congregation is more complete. The passage also addresses an objection about why the author did not mention such hierarchical divisions for the rights of Allah, and responds that the primary categories of qada are the same in number as those of performance (ada), but additional examples can be given for clarification. Overall, this passage establishes the Hanafi rule that in compensation for usurped fungible goods, the identical item is mandatory if available; otherwise, market value is substituted.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): Compensation or fulfillment of a lost obligation, either by its like or value.
المثلي (al-mithli): A fungible good for which a similar item exists in the market without significant difference, e.g., wheat, barley, eggs.
القيمي (al-qimi): A non-fungible good with no standard equivalent, e.g., animals, real estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can compensation by value (qima) be accepted for a usurped fungible (mithli) good?
A) Always, as an alternative to the mithl.
B) Only when the mithl is not available in the market.
C) Only if the owner agrees to accept value.
D) Never; only mithl is valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, identical compensation (mithl) is the primary obligation for fungible goods; value (qima) is only a substitute when the mithl is unavailable.

Qada in the Sense of Ada: Payment of Value in Marriage Dower
Explaining types of judicial payment and retaliation with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qada and ada and apply the rule that paying the value of an unspecified item is considered judicial payment akin to performance in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
When the obligated item is known in genus but unknown in quality, paying its value is qada in the sense of ada.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains the concept of qada that is like ada, using the example of a marriage dower where the husband owes an unspecified slave. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurists treat obligations that are indeterminate in quality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The husband owes a slave as dower without specification. Determine his options: delivering a medium slave (ada) or paying its value (qada).
The ruling is that both are valid, but the wife is compelled to accept either.
2
Classify each option as ada or qada
Delivering the medium slave is clearly ada (performance of the exact obligation). Paying its value is qada (judicial payment), but the text argues it is in the sense of ada.
Why? Because valuation is necessary to determine the medium, so the value stands in for the specific item.
3
Understand the role of valuation
The slave is known in genus but unknown in description. To settle the dispute, a medium must be determined, which requires valuation. Thus, the value becomes the reference.
Valuation transforms the qada into something akin to ada.
4
Derive the legal effect
The wife is compelled to accept the value just as she would accept the specified slave. This shows that qada can be treated as ada in terms of enforceability.
This is a branch (far) on the principle.
5
Link to the usul principle
The principle is that when the obligation is unknown in quality, the qada (value) functions as ada because valuation provides the equivalence. This is a form of qiyas (analogy).
The asl (original case) is delivering a specific slave; the far' (new case) is paying value; the illa (effective cause) is the need to determine the medium.

(السنبلي) في القطع إلخ : قال الشيخ أكمل الدين: هذه المسألة على أوجه؛ لأن القتل إما أن يكون بعد البرء أو قبله فإن كان الأول فإما أن يكون من شخصين، أو شخص واحد عمدين أو خطأين، أو أحدهما خطأ والآخر عمد، وعلى كل فهما جنايتان بالاتفاق، وإن كان الثاني فالقتل من ذلك الشخص أو من شخص آخر، لكن أحدهما كان عمدًا والآخر خطأ، فكذلك أي هما جنايتان، وأما إذا كانا خطأين من شخص واحد فهما جناية واحدة بالاتفاق، وإن كانا عمدين فهو ما نحن فيه. عن القطع عمدا متعلق بكل من القطع والقتل. (القمر) قبل أن يبرأ إلخ أي تحقق القتل قبل صحة الجراحة الحاصلة من القطع، ثم اعلم أنه لابد من ذكر هذا القيد وإن تسامح به المصنف؛ لأن خلاف الإمام وصاحبيه فيما إذا كان الفعلان عمدين و لم يتحقق بينهما برء . (القمر) موجبه أي موجب فعل القاتل وهو القطع ثم القتل. (القمر) لأن موجب إلخ توضيحه أنه إنما يقتص بالقطع إذا ظهر أنه لم يسر إلى القتل، فإذا أفضى إلى القتل العمد دخل موجبه الشرعي أي القصاص في موجب القتل؛ إذا القتل قد أتم أثرًا ثابتا بالقطع، فسقط حكم القطع بنفسه، فصار جناية واحدة بمنزلة ما لو قتل بضربات وليس للولي حينئذ إلا القتل كذا قيل وللإمام أن يقول: إن هذا باعتبار المعنى، وأما من حيث الصورة، فالفعل متعدد وهو القطع والقتل، فالمماثلة الكاملة إنما تحصل بالقطع ثم القطع. (القمر) إذا أفضى إليه إلخ: أما إذا تبين أنه لم يسر إلى القتل لا يقتص إلا بالقطع لحكم النص، وهو قوله تعالى: وَالْجُرُوحَ قِصَاصَ (المائدة: ٤٥) بعد قوله سبحانه: أَنَّ النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْس (المائدة: ٤٥)، وقوله: ﴿فَاعْتَدُوا عَلَيْهِ بِمِثْلِ مَا اعْتَدَى عَلَيْكُمْ﴾ (البقرة: ١٩٤) (السنبلي) أو بالعكس أي الأول خطأ والثاني عمدًا. (القمر) لا يتداخلان أي لا يدخل أحدهما تحت الأخر؛ لأن موجب الأول قد تقرر بالبرء، فيعتبر كل فعل ويؤخذ بموجب الفعلين حتى لو كانا عمدين فللولي القطع والقتل وإن كانا خطأين يجب دية ونصف دية، وإن كان أحدهما عمدًا والآخر خطأ، فإن كان القطع عمدًا والقتل خطأ يجب في اليد القود، وفي النفس الدية، وإن كان القطع خطأ والقتل عمدًا يجب في اليد نصف الدية، وفي النفس القود كذا في "الكفاية". (القمر)
Section on the Specific. Thereby he expressed the explanation of the types of judicial payment and the payment of value in the case where one marries on [the dower of] a slave without specification. This is analogous to the judicial payment which is in the sense of performance, expressed by the word performance: that is, if a man marries a woman on [the dower of] a slave without specification, then if he buys a medium slave and hands it over to her, there is no doubt that it is performance; and if he pays to her the value of a medium slave, this is judicial payment but in the sense of performance, because the slave is known in its essence but unknown in its description. So to settle the dispute, he must hand over a medium slave, and the medium cannot be determined except by valuation, so that the low value is minimum, the high value is maximum, and the medium is between them. So reference is to valuation, therefore the value is in the sense of performance. So that she is compelled to accept it just as if he had brought her the named [slave]. This is a branch on its being in the sense of performance: i.e., the woman is compelled to accept the value just as if he had brought her the specified slave she is compelled to accept the slave; likewise she is compelled to accept the value. Then the author mentioned two branches from Abu Hanifa on his statement, which is the previous one, and said: On this basis Abu Hanifa said regarding retaliation... (Qamar): i.e., because it is in the sense of performance. (Qamar): So this is judicial payment because it is delivery of the equivalent of what is obligatory, i.e., the slave. (Qamar): Therefore etc.: i.e., because value is the reference, value becomes the principal, so delivering it is like delivering the actual obligatory item. (Qamar): By the named: i.e., the slave that he named and specified at the time of marriage. (Qamar): By the specified slave etc.: what is meant is the medium slave, her compulsion to accept is evident: it is pure performance in the case of the slave, and judicial payment in the sense of performance in the case of value. It is known that the husband is given the choice between giving the slave or the value; its reasoning is that delivery is necessary upon him; the slave, in view of being known in genus, is obligatory, and in view of being unknown in description, the value is obligatory, so the obligation by the contract becomes one of two things, so the husband is given a choice, unlike a specific slave because it is known without valuation, so its value becomes pure judicial payment. (Sunbuli) Regarding retaliation etc.: Sheikh Akmal al-Din said: This issue has aspects; because killing is either after cure or before it. If the former, then either from two persons, or one person, both intentional or both accidental, or one accidental and the other intentional; in each case they are two crimes by agreement. If the latter, then the killing by that person or another person, but one of them was intentional and the other accidental, likewise they are two crimes. As for if both are accidental from one person, they are one crime by agreement; and if both are intentional, that is our subject. (Sunbuli) Explanation of the types of judicial payment. Then the intentional killing by the guardian—he does both acts, i.e., because the complete equivalent takes precedence over the deficient equivalent. Abu Hanifa said in the case: A man cuts the hand of a man intentionally, then kills him before it heals: the guardian should do as the killer did—cut him first, then kill him, so that it is requital act for act; since the act is multiple from the killer, it should be likewise from the guardian in observance of the complete equivalent. If he restricts to killing, it is also permissible for him, because he has forgiven part of what is due, so it is as if he forgave all. According to the two companions, the guardian may only exact retaliation by killing, because the liability for cutting was subsumed into the liability for killing when it led to it and no cure intervened. This issue regarding cutting and killing has eight aspects, and the one mentioned in the text is one of them; because either the cutting and killing are both intentional, or both accidental, or the first intentional and the second accidental, or vice versa—these are four. In each case, either cure intervenes between them or not. If the second is after cure, then they are two crimes by agreement, they do not overlap. (Qamar) Regarding cutting intentionally, it is attached to both cutting and killing. (Qamar) Before he heals etc.: i.e., the killing occurs before the healing of the wound caused by the cutting. Know that it is necessary to mention this condition, even if the author is lenient about it, because the difference between the Imam and his two companions is only when both acts are intentional and no cure has occurred between them. (Qamar) Its due: i.e., the due of the killer's act, which is cutting then killing. (Qamar) Because the due etc.: Its clarification: retaliation by cutting is only executed if it is apparent that it did not lead to death; so when it leads to intentional killing, its legal liability (i.e., retaliation) becomes part of the liability for killing, because killing has completed the effect established by cutting, so the ruling of cutting falls by itself, and it becomes one crime like if he killed with multiple blows; then the guardian has only killing. So it is said, and the Imam may say: This is from the perspective of meaning, but from the perspective of form, the act is multiple—cutting and killing—so complete similitude is only achieved by cutting then killing. (Qamar) When it leads to it etc.: As for when it becomes clear that it did not lead to death, he may only exact retaliation by cutting, due to the text of the Quran: 'And wounds are subject to retaliation' (5:45) after His saying: 'That life for life' (5:45), and His saying: 'Then transgress against him the like of his transgression against you' (2:194). (Sunbuli) Or the reverse: i.e., the first accidental and the second intentional. (Qamar) They do not overlap: i.e., one is not subsumed under the other, because the liability for the first has been established by the cure, so each act is considered and both liabilities are taken. So if both are intentional, the guardian has cutting and killing; if both are accidental, full bloodwit and half bloodwit are due; if one is intentional and the other accidental, if the cutting was intentional and killing accidental, then retaliation is due for the hand and bloodwit for the life; if the cutting was accidental and killing intentional, then half bloodwit for the hand and retaliation for the life. Thus in al-Kifaya. (Qamar).
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage from the section on 'al-Khas' (the Specific) in a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary discusses two main legal issues: (1) the nature of payment of value (qayma) in a marriage dower when the slave is unspecified, and (2) the ruling on retaliation (qisas) when a person cuts off a limb and then kills the victim before the wound heals. The first issue examines the distinction between pure performance (ada') and judicial payment (qada) that is like performance. When a husband owes a slave as dower but the slave is not specified, he may either hand over a medium-quality slave (ada') or pay its value (qada), but the value is considered akin to performance because valuation is necessary to determine the medium. The woman is compelled to accept the value just as she would accept the named slave. This illustrates the usul principle that when the obligated item is known in genus but unknown in quality, recourse to valuation transforms the qada into ada'. The second issue is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding retaliation when both cutting and killing are intentional and no cure intervenes. Abu Hanifa holds that the guardian may either cut then kill (for complete similitude) or limit to killing (by forgiving part). The companions hold that only killing is allowed because the liability for cutting merges into the liability for killing. The passage justifies Abu Hanifa's view by emphasizing the multiplicity of acts in form, requiring complete similitude act-for-act. The reasoning (ta'lil) is based on the Quranic verses on retaliation. The passage also outlines eight scenarios based on intentionality and cure, clarifying when acts are separate crimes. This is a typical Hanafi usul dispute where differences in reasoning (ta'lil) lead to different fiqh rulings, illustrating the importance of 'illa (effective cause) in qiyas.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): Judicial payment or compensation that is not the exact specific obligation but is considered equivalent, often requiring valuation
الأداء (al-ada'): Performance of the exact obligation by delivering the precisely specified item or right

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the husband delivers the value of a medium slave instead of the slave itself?
A) The wife may reject it because it is not the specified item.
B) The wife is compelled to accept it because it is qada in the sense of ada.
C) The husband must also deliver a slave; value alone is insufficient.
D) The marriage is invalid because the dower was not specified.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when an obligation is known in genus but unknown in description, paying the value through valuation is considered qada in the sense of ada, making it binding on the creditor.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
